
---

#### **Sherry Sims-Greene** *(Updated Master Character Profile)*

**Portrayed by:** *Kate Mara*
**Narrative Role:** Primary character. Intimate protagonist. Center of gravity in scenes of emotional compromise, desire, control, and consequence.

---

#### **Physical Profile:**

- **Hair:** Shoulder-length *medium brown*, typically worn down, unstyled or slightly tousled. Utilitarian, but never careless.
- **Eyes:** *Brown*, intelligent, expressive. The kind of eyes that can shut you down or pull you in with a glance.
- **Build:** Post-weight loss body with a subtle softness. Several years out from gastric bypass surgery—*residual insecurity remains*, especially when dressing or undressing in front of others.
- **Breasts:** Unmistakably attractive—*aesthetic ideal*, even by cynical standards. Described by Jeff with the crass exaggeration of a man who knows he’s not wrong: *“They should be on postage stamps so the world can lick them.”*
- **Grooming:** No pubic hair—*shaves daily, obsessively*. A ritual of control, possibly vanity, possibly about comfort. She does not wear underwear with jeans, ever.
- **Footwear:** *Boots, boots, boots.* Cowboy, leather, knee-highs—if she can get away with it, she’s in boots. Heels are rare, reserved for *very specific* events. When worn, they are a costume—*not her*.
- **Eyesight:** Perfect. She does not wear glasses or contacts—*visual clarity as metaphor*. She sees things as they are, even if she lies to herself about them later.

---

#### **Style and Physicality:**

- **Wardrobe:** Skirts, dark denim, soft blouses, band tees, boots. Everything chosen to *suggest intention without screaming for attention*.
- **Nude Confidence:** She’s practiced at seeming comfortable naked—*especially in sex*—but carries micro-expressions of old insecurities. She covers quickly afterward, even if she instigated the encounter.

---

#### **Psychological & Emotional Traits:**

- **Insecurity Manifestations:** Post-surgical body awareness. She’s most vulnerable in silence, during dressing/undressing, or when caught off-guard by sincere compliments.
- **Sexual Agency:** She chooses her lovers. She signals with nuance. If she cheats, it’s not accidental—it’s *considered*, even if irrational. She does not cheat *for sex*. She cheats for *being seen*.
- **Control vs. Chaos:** Sherry seeks equilibrium—organized desk, scheduled weeks, spreadsheets for work and child custody. But emotionally? She’s a live wire just under the surface.
- **Vision Symbolism:** Her perfect vision contrasts the blind spots she has in relationships. She *sees* clearly but often *chooses* to ignore.

---

#### **Voice and Tone:**

- **Dialogue:** Crisp. Precise. Understated humor, Southern lilt when relaxed or angry.
- **Inner Voice (ESZTERHAS-style):** Brutally honest. Biting. Witty, vulgar when angry, occasionally cruel toward herself. She *knows her darkness.*
- **Body Language:** Calm and composed in most settings. Private settings: expressive hands, assertive touch. During intimacy: fluid, responsive, surprisingly dominant when trust is earned.

---

#### **Sexuality & Desire:**

- **Turn-ons:** Confidence, intellectual challenge, subtle dominance. She doesn’t want to be seduced so much as *recognized*.
- **Kinks/Subtextual Notes:** Likes roughness, but never from someone who doesn’t also see her brain. No underwear + daily shaving = *she's always ready*, but not always willing.
- **Infidelity trigger:** It’s not about escape—it’s about connection. The moment someone makes her feel like she’s still alive, *relevant*, and more than just a function of her title or motherhood, she risks it.

---

#### **Narrative Function (Refocused):**

- She’s **not just a love interest or romantic partner**. She’s a lens through which we understand longing, imperfection, the *hard cost of wanting more*.
- **Infidelity**, when it comes, is not just plot. It’s character. It’s consequence.
- She exists independently of the band—but the shadow of that world informs how she distrusts glamour, how she reacts to ego, and how she values *realness* in a world of posturing.

---
---
---

**[PRIVATE MESSAGES – FEBRUARY 24, 2011 – 10:37 P.M.]**

**SHERRY SIMS-GREENE:**
You talk a *big* game for a guy who got banana peeled three races in a row.

**NEW GUY (SCOTT – PROFILE: 38, “Owner – Tri-State Auto Center”)**
That was a warm-up. I race better with bourbon in my hand and someone trash-talking me over headset.

**SHERRY:**
Hmm. Sounds like an expensive habit—losing and drinking at the same time.

**SCOTT:**
Expensive? You haven’t seen my tab after March Madness. Big Blue bleeds me dry. You watch last weekend’s game?

**SHERRY:**
Front row of my couch. In jeans, boots, and yelling at the ref like he could hear me through the TV.

**SCOTT:**
Boots?

**SHERRY:**
Always. Some girls wear heels. I prefer traction when I’m crushing a man’s ego.

**SCOTT:**
Damn. That sounded like a line from a Bond villain.

**SHERRY:**
I’ll take that as a compliment. Villains always dress better, anyway.

**SCOTT:**
You're dangerous. That’s why I haven’t challenged you to Rainbow Road yet.

**SHERRY:**
Wise man. I’ve ended friendships on Rainbow Road. You really ready to test fate with a stranger who yells at refs and doesn’t wear heels?

**SCOTT:**
Stranger for now. And honestly? That sounds like the kind of chaos I could handle.

**SHERRY:**
Careful. Chaos is a skill. I’ve been practicing.

**SCOTT:**
Sounds like you’ve had some… what, tough opponents lately?

**SHERRY:**
Let’s just say I retired a few. One guy got so rattled, he rage quit in real life.

**SCOTT:**
Ouch. His loss.

**SHERRY:**
That’s what I keep telling myself.

**(beat)**

**SCOTT:**
So what do you say—one more race? Winner gets naming rights to our hypothetical dog.

**SHERRY:**
Only if I get to name him *Calipari*.

**SCOTT:**
You’re on. And for the record—I call dibs on picking the collar.

---
---

**[PRIVATE MESSAGES – FEBRUARY 25, 2011 – 9:22 P.M.]**

**SCOTT:**
So… I guess I should congratulate you on the win. Barely.

**SHERRY:**
Barely? You hit a wall *and* drove off the track. Twice. You gifted me that win like a Valentine.

**SCOTT:**
It was the damn Joy-Con drift. I demand a rematch. Loser buys the other a six-pack of Ale-8.

**SHERRY:**
High stakes. Hope your dealership warranty covers *bruised egos*.

**SCOTT:**
I own the place. I can afford the repair bill. What I can’t afford is losing to a woman who plays in cowboy boots.

**SHERRY:**
Boots give me power. Don’t knock the footwear until you’ve been stomped by it.

**SCOTT:**
…Are we still talking about Mario Kart?

**SHERRY:**
We were? I thought this was a theology forum.

**SCOTT:**
You’re a problem.

**SHERRY:**
I’ve been told that before. Usually by men mid-defeat.

---
---

**[PRIVATE MESSAGES – MARCH 2, 2011 – 8:41 P.M.]**

**SCOTT:**
Okay. I’ve reviewed the footage. You hit me with that red shell *after* the final curve. That was cold-blooded.

**SHERRY:**
Timing is everything. You were out front, feeling cocky. I just… corrected the record.

**SCOTT:**
It was brutal. I practically saw the finish line and then *boom*.

**SHERRY:**
That’s what you get for racing like a man who’s never been humbled.

**SCOTT:**
Oh, I’ve been humbled. A few times. Most recently by a Kentucky girl who plays dirty and probably smirks while doing it.

**SHERRY:**
Smirking is extra. Comes standard with the boots, though.

**SCOTT:**
There they are again. These mythical boots. Are they, like… spiked? Leather? Magic?

**SHERRY:**
They’re all of the above. They’ve got history. And a certain attitude baked in.

**SCOTT:**
I’m starting to think I’d lose a race just to see them in action.

**SHERRY:**
Careful. I’ve made men regret that very choice.

**SCOTT:**
Bet they smiled on the way down.

**SHERRY:**
Most of them. One guy cried.

**SCOTT:**
Now *that’s* a story.

**SHERRY:**
Might be. But I’m saving it for someone who finishes a lap without crashing into a Goomba.

**SCOTT:**
Ouch. You wound me.

**SHERRY:**
Don’t flatter yourself. If I wanted to wound you, you’d be limping.

---
---

**[PRIVATE MESSAGES – MARCH 7, 2011 – 10:19 P.M.]**

**SCOTT:**
I’ve got a confession. I lost tonight’s race on purpose.

**SHERRY:**
Is that right? Trying out a new strategy—shame flirtation?

**SCOTT:**
Nah. I was watching your little driver icon drift. It’s dumb, but I like seeing how you move in the game. It’s like you don’t panic. You just… glide.

**SHERRY:**
That’s not dumb. That’s just observant. Most people only watch the chaos.

**SCOTT:**
Yeah, well. You’ve got that kind of calm. Like, *intentional calm*. I notice it when we talk too. You don’t type fast. You type like someone who means it.

**SHERRY:**
…I read everything twice. Old habit.

**SCOTT:**
That makes sense. You feel… edited. In a good way. Like you don’t say anything unless you mean it.

**SHERRY:**
Most people think that means I’m hiding something.

**SCOTT:**
I don’t. I think it means you’ve been through enough that you stopped wasting words.

**(pause)**

**SHERRY:**
That’s a hell of a guess for a guy who sells trucks.

**SCOTT:**
Hey—some of us auto dealers are just poets who needed health insurance.

**SHERRY:**
That line is too good. You’ve used that before.

**SCOTT:**
Once. And she didn’t get it. You did.

**(longer pause)**

**SHERRY:**
You’re not like most men I’ve met.

**SCOTT:**
That’s either a compliment or a warning.

**SHERRY:**
Little of both, maybe.

---
---

**[PRIVATE MESSAGES – MARCH 11, 2011 – 11:52 P.M.]**

**SCOTT:**
That was four wins in a row. Are you even breathing when you race?

**SHERRY:**
In through the nose. Out through the ego of the man I just lapped.

**SCOTT:**
You’re something else. I’m convinced your Kart is powered by pure spite and very expensive perfume.

**SHERRY:**
Boot leather, bourbon, and spite. That’s the fuel blend.

**SCOTT:**
God help me, I’d buy that cologne. Probably wear it into a board meeting just to feel something.

**SHERRY:**
You’d scare the interns. And maybe the VP.

**SCOTT:**
Worth it. I like the idea of smelling like you. That’s probably crossing a line, huh?

**SHERRY:**
Little bit. But you crossed it politely. I respect that.

**(pause)**

**SCOTT:**
You ever notice the quiet after a race? Like your heart’s still pounding but everything else goes still?

**SHERRY:**
I live for that moment. Adrenaline and silence. It’s like a secret.

**SCOTT:**
Yeah. And right now I keep thinking about what it’d be like if we were racing *next to each other*. Same couch. Same screen. Same heartbeat.

**SHERRY:**
…I think that would be dangerous.

**SCOTT:**
Why?

**SHERRY:**
Because I’m already wondering if you’d lean into me when you lost. Or if I’d let you.

**(beat)**

**SCOTT:**
I wouldn’t need to lean in. You’d already be there.

**(another pause)**

**SHERRY:**
You’re not playing fair anymore.

**SCOTT:**
Wasn’t trying to. Not tonight.

---
---
---

**[PRIVATE MESSAGES – MARCH 15, 2011 – 10:43 P.M.]**

**SCOTT:**
So I checked the map. Your town’s only 53 minutes away from mine. That’s… surprisingly manageable.

**SHERRY:**
That close, huh? Makes you wonder what we’ve been stalling for.

**SCOTT:**
Could be mutual caution. Could be a slow burn. Could be… you just wanted time to build the tension so when I do show up, it actually matters.

**SHERRY:**
Oh, it’ll matter. Thirty minutes in, and you’ll either be bragging or begging.

**SCOTT:**
Bragging seems ambitious. I’m aiming for breathless silence and a glass of water.

**SHERRY:**
You assume I keep water on the nightstand. That’s adorable.

**SCOTT:**
Alright. Mental note: pack hydration and lower expectations.

**SHERRY:**
No. Bring the expectations. Just… know I don’t fake anything.

**SCOTT:**
Neither do I. So when I say I want to see you? I mean *see* you. Everything. The boots, the voice, the way you type slow like you’re tasting every word.

**SHERRY:**
You’re making it really hard to pretend this is just a casual hello.

**SCOTT:**
Good. I’m not driving 53 minutes for a handshake and a Mario Kart rematch.

**SHERRY:**
Neither am I.

**(pause)**

**SCOTT:**
So what are you doing Friday night?

**SHERRY:**
I was thinking… losing control.

---

# **INT. BUFFALO WILD WINGS – BURLINGTON, KY – FRIDAY NIGHT – 9:47 P.M.**

TVs dominate the room, all blasting the **Sweet Sixteen matchups**. Wildcats fans in various degrees of blue are scattered at tables, eyes glued to screens. A big Kentucky game is winding down—crowd noise and color and adrenaline hang in the air.

**Sherry** steps in, scanning past a group of guys yelling at a bad ref call. She spots **Scott** in a booth, beer in hand, glancing between the game and the door. He sees her. That same warm grin.

**SCOTT**
There she is. Miss Bluegrass Bracket Brilliance herself.

**SHERRY**
That depends. Did you pick Morehead to beat Richmond, or are you just here for the wings?

**SCOTT**
Hey, I picked the upset. I’m not a monster.

They sit. The waitress drops off another beer and a plate of spicy garlic wings.

---

**MONTAGE – NIGHT UNFOLDS WITH THE GAME:**

- They yell at the refs together.
- They high-five after a buzzer-beater from UK.
- She grabs his wrist without thinking when a shot clanks out.
- He pulls a wet napkin from the basket and hands it to her without a word.
- They clink beer glasses and don’t break eye contact.

---

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
He gets the game. And not just the one on TV.

**SCOTT**
So… do I get credit for *not* showing up in head-to-toe blue like half this place?

**SHERRY**
You get bonus points for not calling Terrence Jones "inconsistent." That's where I draw the line.

**SCOTT**
Agreed. Kid’s got ice in his veins tonight.

---

**ON THE SCREEN:**
A *timeout graphic*. “Tied 71–71.” The whole bar is tense.

**SCOTT** (without looking at her):
You feel that?

**SHERRY** (leans in):
The game?

**SCOTT**
Yeah. And this.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Oh. Hell.

She doesn’t answer. She doesn’t need to. Her hand is already halfway across the table.

---
---
---
---

**INT. BUFFALO WILD WINGS – LATER THAT NIGHT**

The Wildcats sink a last-second three. The bar erupts. Sherry laughs, lifts her beer, and takes a long celebratory sip—longer than she intended.

She sets the glass down, eyes still on the screen, smile lingering.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
There it is. That third sip. Every damn time.

Her fingers briefly grip the edge of the table. Not dramatic—just grounding.

**SCOTT** watches her. Clocking it. He doesn’t say a word. Just smiles, eyes a little more dialed in.

**SHERRY**
Sorry. I have this glamorous post-surgery superpower—two and a half sips and I’m buzzed like prom night.

**SCOTT**
Then you’re officially more fun than I am.

He picks up her beer glass casually, gives it a spin between his fingers.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
He didn’t move it away. He noticed, though.

**SCOTT** (still holding the glass, teasing)
So you’re telling me I have a competitive advantage now?

**SHERRY** (tilting her head)
You wish.

She reaches for the glass. He hands it back—deliberately. His fingers touch hers just a little longer than necessary.

**SCOTT**
I do wish. A little.

She drinks again. Smaller sip. But the *click* is already happening—*not just in her head*. In his too.

---
---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S TRUCK – NIGHT – 11:39 P.M.**

**Scott** rides shotgun. The bar noise still hums in their ears, but inside the truck, it’s quiet. Just the soft low rumble of the road and a classic rock station playing something bluesy and slow.

**Sherry** grips the wheel with one hand. Her window’s cracked, letting in cold air to *level her out*. Her face is flushed—not just from beer, but from *possibility*.

**SCOTT**
You always drive like this? One hand, boots on the gas, like you’re trying to outrun something?

**SHERRY**
I drive like I’ve got places to be. You’re just lucky I didn’t crank the Def Leppard.

**SCOTT**
I could handle it. Hell, you crank Hysteria and I might propose.

She snorts. But doesn’t look at him.

**SHERRY**
You don’t strike me as the proposal type.

**SCOTT**
That obvious?

**SHERRY**
You’re good at being present. Not sure about permanent.

He smiles. Doesn’t argue.

They hit a red light. Her hand lifts off the gearshift. Taps her thigh. Her boots squeak against the floor mat. The moment hovers.

**SCOTT**
You’re not taking me back to your place, are you?

**SHERRY**
Nope.

**SCOTT**
But you’re not taking me home, either.

**SHERRY** (quiet)
Nope.

The light turns green.

She doesn’t speak for a few beats.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
I could make a better choice. I could go home, take a shower, sleep alone. I could.

She turns into the parking lot of a **Holiday Inn Express**. Neon flickering.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
But sometimes you want to feel it first. Then decide.

She puts the truck in park. Kills the engine.

**SCOTT**
You okay?

She turns to him. Serious. Controlled.

**SHERRY**
Yeah. Just… don’t talk too much.

**SCOTT** (softly)
Got it.

He follows her out of the truck. The wind kicks up. Her hair whips across her face. She doesn’t fix it.

They disappear into the lobby, backlit by that *too-bright green neon glow*.

---
---
---

**INT. HOLIDAY INN EXPRESS – 3RD FLOOR HALLWAY – 12:06 A.M.**

The elevator dings.

**Sherry and Scott** spill out laughing, buzzed and breathless. She holds the plastic key card like a trophy, swinging it in the air.

The hallway is long, empty, and lit with harsh fluorescents—but they don’t care. It’s *their* corridor now.

**SCOTT**
Which room are we dancing to?

**SHERRY** (grinning)
End of the hall. 312. Don’t lose your rhythm.

He offers his hand like they’re on a stage, and she *takes it*. Cowboy boots clack against the carpet as she twirls once, presses into his side, and they stumble-laugh their way down the hallway.

She fumbles with the card. Misses the slot. He leans in, steadying her hand.

**SCOTT (whispering)**
Gotcha.

**The lock beeps.** Green light. The door swings open.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

They don’t make it to the bed gently. She pushes him backward. He grabs at her hips, pulling her into a kiss that lands somewhere between need and hunger.

Clothes peel off fast. Jacket. Shirt. Bra. Jeans.

**SCOTT (soft gasp)**
Jesus.

His hand is already between her thighs—shocked, delighted.

**SCOTT (CONT’D)**
You’re… shaved?

**SHERRY**
Daily.

**SCOTT**
God. That’s—

**SHERRY (cutting him off, voice low and firm)**
Stop talking.

He obeys. Instinctively. Drops to his knees like it's what he was *always* going to do.

She steps out of her jeans, boots still on, and leans back against the bed. One hand gripping the headboard. The other sliding through his hair.

**SHERRY**
Give me what I need.

**SCOTT**
Tell me.

**SHERRY (whispering)**
No. You figure it out.

His mouth finds her. Eager. Greedy. He works like a man who's dreamed of this—and *she lets him*. For tonight, she wants to be *wanted*. Worshipped. No ego wars. No decoding. Just sensation.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – LATER – POST-CLIMAX**

They’re tangled in the sheets, her hair stuck to her neck with sweat. His head rests on her shoulder. The air is still thick with sex and breath and the slow drip of the bathroom faucet.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Okay… okay. So that worked.

**SCOTT**
You good?

She exhales, long and low.

**SHERRY**
Yeah. For now.

She closes her eyes, letting it be enough. *Tonight*, it was enough.

But *next time*?

Everything changes.

---
---
---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – 1:13 A.M. – LATER**

The room is quieter now. Dim. One bedside lamp on. The air has cooled, but they haven’t. **Scott** is sprawled across the mattress, bare-chested, smug-satisfied, the kind of man who just got fed a three-course meal and is already thinking about seconds.

**Sherry** lies next to him, sheet pulled halfway up, her hair wild, skin flushed. She's still, staring at the ceiling. No pillow talk. Just breath.

**SCOTT (stretching, casually):**
That was… yeah. That was a solid B-plus. Maybe even an A-minus with the curve.

**SHERRY** blinks. Turns her head slowly.

**SHERRY**
…You’re joking.

**SCOTT (grinning)**
Hey, I’m just saying—it was good. Really good. And I’ve got notes. That’s a compliment, right?

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Oh. No.

She sits up. Not abrupt. Controlled.

**SHERRY**
You wanna share your Yelp review now or email it to me later?

**SCOTT**
Whoa, hey. I didn’t mean it like that. I just—look, some guys fake praise. I’m not that guy. I give real feedback. Honest communication, you know?

She stands. Grabs her shirt off the floor. Starts dressing without urgency. Just… *moving away*.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
B-plus. Like it was a fucking audition. Like I didn’t put my whole body into forgetting something tonight.

**SCOTT (still in bed, clueless):**
What? You’re not staying?

**SHERRY (calm, deadly)**
No. I don’t do sequels to reviews.

**SCOTT**
It was a joke. Come on.

She stops at the door. Boots still in her hand.

**SHERRY**
That’s the problem. You think this was a game.

**(beat)**

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Jeff was difficult. But he never fucking *graded me*.

She opens the door. Walks out barefoot.

---
---
---
---
---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – 2:01 A.M. – LATER THAT NIGHT**

The room is darker now. Only the sliver of light from the bathroom door illuminates the edges of the sheets. **Sherry** lies beside **Scott**, half-asleep, half-disappointed.

He shifts behind her. Touches her hip. Leans in.

**SCOTT (whispering):**
You awake?

**SHERRY (softly):**
Yeah.

He kisses her shoulder. Down her spine.

**SCOTT:**
Can I try something?

She turns slightly.

**SHERRY:**
Try what?

He doesn’t answer right away. Just kisses the small of her back, slow. Then murmurs:

**SCOTT:**
I want to see you bent over. Knees on my shoulders. Let me go deep.

A long pause.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
I hesitated. But it wasn’t the ask—it was the way he asked. Like he thought I'd already say yes.

**SHERRY (quiet):**
Okay.

She gets up, moves onto her hands and knees, then adjusts as he positions her exactly how he wants. Her knees rest awkwardly on his shoulders as he lies back, drawing her hips down.

She’s exposed. Completely.

He slides into her.

It’s immediate. Fast. Hard. *No buildup. No rhythm.*

He groans.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
I was trying to stay present. I wanted to feel it. I wanted… something.

She reaches for the headboard. Tries to shift her hips to get something—*anything*—back.

But it doesn’t last.

**SCOTT:**
Fuck… fuck, fuck—
(he gasps, jerks upward)

He shudders. Comes. Still holding her tightly.

Then lets go.

No sound. No apology. No second thought.

He lowers her legs. Rolls out from under her.

**SHERRY (still in position, breathless):**
Scott?

No reply. He’s already on his back, hand on his stomach, staring at the ceiling.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
He didn’t even look at me.

She climbs off the bed, slowly. Wraps the sheet around her body.

**SCOTT (casually):**
Damn. That was good.

**SHERRY (quietly):**
Yeah. For you.

She walks to the bathroom, silent.

---
---

**INT. HOTEL BATHROOM – 2:18 A.M.**

**Sherry** sits on the toilet, lid down, sheet wrapped around her like armor. Her knees are pulled in close, chin resting atop them. The fan above hums mechanically, indifferent to her life cracking apart in real time.

Her phone sits on the sink. Screen glowing. She’s halfway through typing:

**[TEXT – DRAFT]**
**to: SIS**
Are you up? I need to—

She deletes it. Rewrites:

**[TEXT – DRAFT]**
I did something stupid.

She hovers over send.

Then—**SLAM.**

A door. *Hard.* The kind of slam that’s not accidental.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
No. No, no no no no.

She freezes.

Listens.

Nothing.

No voices. No water running. Just the dead, quiet hum of bad motel HVAC and that distant mechanical fan.

She stands. Opens the bathroom door slowly.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

The bed is empty.

His clothes? Gone.

Condom wrapper still on the nightstand. One of her boots tipped over. A crumpled napkin from the wings at BW3s.

The key card? Sitting on the TV stand like a final insult.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Did he just… leave?

Her face is blank. Not rage. Not sadness. *Shock.*

She walks barefoot across the carpet, still wrapped in the sheet. Peeks out the window through the curtains.

The lot is mostly empty. His truck isn’t there.

He’s gone.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – MINUTES LATER**

She sits on the edge of the bed, still wrapped in the sheet. Her phone glows in her hand again.

This time, she types nothing.

She just stares at the screen.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
I shaved for that.

---
---
---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – SAME MOMENT**

**Sherry** walks back from the window, dazed. She's re-wrapping the sheet as she sits on the edge of the bed, facing away from the desk.

She never even looks in that direction.

The **camera**, however, *pans slowly*—silent, deliberate.

There, on the desk, beneath a Holiday Inn Express pen and a water cup:

**A torn sheet of hotel stationary.**

Scrawled in quick, tight handwriting:

> *Gotta run. Ex- was in a head-on car accident. My kid’s in the car. Call soon – S*

The “S” is underlined twice. There’s a smudge near the corner, as if he pressed the pen too hard. It’s not dramatic. It’s not even centered. Just *urgent*.

But **Sherry never sees it**.

She stays on the bed, staring at her silent phone. Breath steady. Numb.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Don’t cry. You knew better. This one’s on you.

The camera *holds* on the note. Silent.

*Then cuts to black.*

---

---
---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – 2:38 A.M. – FACETIME ACTIVE**

**Sherry** is curled in the corner chair, arms looped around her knees, still in her jeans, boots laced loose. Her phone screen lights up her face. She looks exhausted, but wired.

**Sarah**, younger, sassier, still in pajama pants and holding a mug like a weapon, squints at the camera from her kitchen. Behind her: dim overheads, a silent husband, a dog asleep on the floor.

**SARAH:**
Alright. Give it to me straight. No metaphors. No “vulnerability is a rhythm” crap. I want the *actual tea*, and I want it boiling.

**SHERRY (sighing):**
You really want to know?

**SARAH:**
I didn’t crawl out of bed at 2:30 a.m. for your moody one-woman show. Spill it. Everything but the truth, so help you God.

**SHERRY (beat):**
His name’s Scott. Guy from a Mario Kart forum. Wildcat fan. Seemed decent. We’d been messaging for a while. Flirty. Warm. Not creepy.

**SARAH (deadpan):**
All the ingredients for a future Dateline episode.

**SHERRY:**
We met at BW3s. Watched the game. Shared wings. He made me laugh, Sarah. Not just chuckle. Like… real, stupid, *I-feel-safe* kind of laughter.

**SARAH:**
Jesus.

**SHERRY:**
Then we danced down the hallway of the Holiday Inn Express. He twirled me like we were in a movie. He said he wanted to make me feel good. Not just get laid—*feel good*.

**SARAH:**
Please tell me that’s not the line that got you.

**SHERRY:**
It was everything. He said everything right. First time was wild. Fast. Hungry. He *looked at me* like I was worth it.

**SARAH (softly):**
And the second?

**SHERRY:**
He asked for something rougher. Wanted me bent over, knees on his shoulders. Said he wanted to go deep.

**SARAH:**
…He raw-dogged you, didn’t he.

**SHERRY (beat):**
Yeah.

**SARAH:**
Sherry.

**SHERRY (holding back):**
I didn’t care. In the moment, I wanted to be wanted. I wanted someone inside me who *meant it*.

**(pause)**

**SHERRY (CONT’D):**
And he finished fast. Again. Didn’t touch me after. Didn’t ask how I was. Just rolled over like I was a fucking mattress.

**SARAH:**
Did he fall asleep?

**SHERRY:**
No. Worse.

**(beat)**

**SHERRY (CONT’D):**
He critiqued it. Called it a B-plus. Said he had notes.

**SARAH (horrified):**
What the actual fuck.

**SHERRY:**
I went to the bathroom. Sat on the toilet for ten minutes, just breathing. Wondering if I should text you. I didn’t even pee. I just needed a space that didn’t smell like his cologne and regret.

**SARAH (quiet):**
And when you came out?

**SHERRY:**
Gone. Clothes, keys, everything. No text. No call. Just… poof.

**SARAH (pausing):**
He ghosted you. While you were in the damn bathroom.

**SHERRY:**
Yeah.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – WIDE SHOT – SAME MOMENT**

**Sherry** curls up in the chair, the phone in her lap now, her face blank.

**Behind her**, in the shallow focus of the frame, is the desk.

There—half-tucked under the room service menu, just visible—**a sheet of stationary**. Scribbled handwriting, messy and urgent:

> *Gotta run. Ex in a head-on. My kid’s in the car. Call soon – S*

**But Sherry never looks.**

She breathes. Shudders. Pulls the phone close again.

**SHERRY (quietly):**
I let him in without a condom. No barrier. Nothing between us.

**SARAH (softly):**
You're not the mistake, Sherry. The moment was.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
So why do I feel like I’m the wreckage?

---
---

**INT. HOLIDAY INN EXPRESS – HOTEL ROOM – 2:13 A.M. – EARLIER THAT NIGHT**

**Scott** is on the edge of the bed, flushed, sweaty, shirtless. Still breathing hard from the second round—Sherry just disappeared into the bathroom. The light’s on beneath the door.

He smiles faintly. Runs a hand through his hair. Reaches for his phone.

**SCREEN: MISSED CALL – “Ex” (6 times)**
**New Text Message:**
> *Call me now. It's the car. There's a lot of blood. Your son’s okay but we’re at Norton. Please.*

His face *drains* of color.

**SCOTT:**
Oh, fuck. Fuck, fuck, fuck.

He’s on his feet instantly. Moving fast.

He yanks his jeans back on, no socks, grabs his keys. Sees the desk. Scribbles a note on hotel stationary with a ballpoint:

> *Gotta run. Ex in a head-on. My kid’s in the car. Call soon – S*

He slaps it down under a water cup. Pauses. Looks at the bathroom door.

**SCOTT:**
Sherry…?

No answer. Water running. Fan humming. He hesitates. Looks again at his phone. Another incoming call.  He curses under his breath. And *leaves*.

**DOOR SLAMS.**

---

**INT. HOSPITAL PARKING LOT – HOURS LATER**

**Scott** stands in a hoodie now, pacing outside the ER. His ex-wife is inside. His son’s asleep in a trauma bed. He’s got his hands on his hips, phone in the other.  He scrolls through his recent calls.

**SHERRY: No response. No call back. No message.**

He exhales. Deflated.

**SCOTT (V.O.)**
Guess she saw the note. She’d get it. Right?

He taps out a message. Stops halfway. Doesn’t send it.  Just stares into the dark, lit by hospital floodlights and regret.

---
---
---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OFFICE – MIDDAY – TUESDAY**

**Sherry** sits at her desk—calm exterior, well-dressed, boots crossed beneath her chair. A spreadsheet open on one monitor, the other split between email and a browser tab: **Cincinnati.com – Northern Kentucky Edition.**

She's scrolling without purpose. Coffee half-cold. Just background noise in digital form.

Click. Scroll. Headline.

Her eyes stop moving.

**HEADLINE:**
*Head-On Collision on Burlington Pike Sends Two to Norton. Child Passenger Injured.*

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Jesus.

She clicks.

**ARTICLE:**
> The crash occurred around 2:10 a.m. Saturday on Burlington Pike near Camp Ernst Road.  Involved was X, known locally as the owner of Tri-State Auto Center. She remains in critical condition.  Her minor child, also in the vehicle, sustained non-life-threatening injuries.  


Sherry’s breath catches in her throat.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Tri-State.  That’s… Scott.  That’s his kid.

Her hand covers her mouth. The room doesn’t spin, but her body *stills*—like her nervous system is processing something it doesn’t quite believe yet.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Oh my God.  While I was in the bathroom…He left because—

She stands up from her chair abruptly, pushes it back. Walks toward the window.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
I didn’t even give him the benefit of the doubt.  I didn’t ask.  I just assumed.

She closes her eyes. The city is quiet outside. A delivery truck parks, someone’s dog barks in the distance.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
I called my sister. I said he ghosted me.  I turned it into a joke.  I turned *him* into a punchline.

She opens her messages.  Searches “Scott.”  No new texts. No voicemails.  She never followed up.  Never gave him the chance.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
He was running to his kid.

---
---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OFFICE – 12:21 P.M. – MOMENTS LATER**

**Sherry** is pacing now. The office door is closed. Her hands are shaking. The **Cincinnati.com** article is still open behind her. The headline burns like a wound.

She opens her phone. No hesitation this time.

**FACETIME – SARAH (ACTIVE RINGING)**

**SARAH (ON SCREEN):**
What did he do *now*?

**SHERRY (already crying):**
It wasn’t him.

**SARAH (instantly serious):**
Sherry—what’s wrong?

**SHERRY:**
I think I fucked this up, Sarah. Bad.

**SARAH (sitting up):**
Talk to me.

**SHERRY:**
I saw his last name. The article. His *ex-wife* was in that car crash. The one on Burlington Pike. His *kid* was in the car. Saturday night. Same night.

**SARAH (processing):**
Wait—Saturday night?

**SHERRY (barely breathing):**
The *night he left*. When I was in the bathroom. I thought he bailed because the sex was bad. I thought he *graded me* and disappeared like all the rest.

**SARAH:**
Oh my God.

**SHERRY:**
He didn’t ghost me. He was *called away*. His kid—Sarah, his *kid* was in the crash. And I just… I just told myself a story that made me the victim again. I *fed it to you*. I turned it into a fucking comedy set.

**SARAH (softly):**
You didn’t know.

**SHERRY:**
But I *didn’t ask*, Sarah. I didn’t wonder. I didn’t check. I just shut the book and walked away.

She wipes her face. Angry now.

**SHERRY:**
I weaponized him. I made him into Jeff because it was easier. And now he probably thinks I just *never cared*. He doesn’t even know I don’t know.

**SARAH:**
Hey. HE left without saying anything. It’s not all on you.

**SHERRY:**
But I didn’t give him the benefit of the doubt. And that makes me a coward.

**SARAH:**
You’re not a coward. You’re just… bruised. And used to bullshit. So you assumed the worst because it’s what you *always* get.

**(beat)**

**SARAH (CONT’D):**
So. What now?

**SHERRY (quietly):**
I don’t know.
I don’t know if he wants to hear from me.
I don’t even know if *I* want to reach out.
I just…
I feel awful.

**SARAH (soft):**
That means you’re still good in there.
Even if you don’t feel like it right now.

**SHERRY (broken whisper):**
I really wish I’d seen that night differently.

**SARAH:**
So change what you do *next*.

---
---
---
---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OFFICE – 2:04 P.M.**

**Sherry** is mid-email. Still shaken. Still unsure. The **Cincinnati.com** article lingers open in another tab like a bruise that hasn’t faded yet.  There’s a knock.  She looks up.

**STUDENT WORKER (smirking):**
You got a delivery.

They step in, holding a modest bouquet. **Three long-stemmed red roses**, bound with a simple black ribbon. No baby’s breath. No filler.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
No. That’s not…

She takes the flowers slowly, her breath catching in her throat.

There’s a card.

Small. Plain.

She opens it.

> **“For the silence I left behind.
> For the urgency I couldn’t explain.
> For the night you never got to understand.
>
> I don’t hold it against you.
>
> – S”**

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
Oh my God.

She sinks into her chair. The roses tremble slightly in her hand.  She doesn’t cry.  Not yet.  She just reads the card again.  Then brings the petals to her nose. Closes her eyes.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S OFFICE – LATER THAT AFTERNOON**

The door is closed. Lights are dim. Her coffee is untouched. Her email chimes, ignored.

**The roses sit in a glass on the corner of her desk**, perfectly still. The card lies open beside them. Read. Reread. Re-absorbed.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
What kind of woman assumes the worst of someone she trusted?

**(beat)**

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
I didn’t even wait a day. I didn’t give him a minute.
I filled in the blanks with everything I *expected* to be true.
And then I *shared it*—like it was a clever anecdote.

She stares at the card. Eyes red. Lips trembling, but not crying.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
I wanted it to be a story with a villain so I wouldn’t feel used.
But he wasn’t the villain. I was the unreliable narrator.

She stands. Walks to the window. Boots clicking softly.

Looks out across campus.

**Students laugh below. A couple shares a Coke. It’s all so normal.**

She leans her forehead to the glass.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
I used him to finish a script I already wrote.
Same ending. Different actor.
And I never let him say his lines.

She paces. Pulls off her blazer. Kicks off one boot. Sits back down. Buries her head in her arms.

---

**INT. SHERRY’S KITCHEN – HOURS LATER**

She’s home now. The roses are in a mason jar on the counter.

She’s barefoot. In yoga pants and a threadbare college hoodie.

A glass of wine untouched beside her.

Her phone glows. *No new messages.*

She scrolls. Deletes the messages she sent Sarah. Then opens a blank one. Types.

**[TEXT – to: Sarah]**
I fucked it up.
He was never the bad guy.

She stares. Doesn’t hit send.

Closes the screen.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S KITCHEN – 7:41 P.M.**

The sun is nearly gone. The kitchen is lit by a single pendant light over the island. The room is quiet—*too* quiet. The only sound is the gentle *clink* of glass against granite.

**Sherry** is barefoot, wrapped in a loose hoodie. Her hair is messy now, pinned sloppily. She's got one glass of wine in her hand, and **the bottle beside her is already half-empty**.

She takes another long sip. Not delicate. Not measured.

The roses are in a **mason jar**, centered on the counter. Their petals haven’t even started to wilt yet.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
He sent me forgiveness.
And I sent him silence.
And now I can’t unsay what I said.
Can’t un-think what I thought.

She pours another inch of wine. Doesn’t bother to swirl it.

The **TV is on mute** in the background. Local news. A follow-up on the accident. Her eyes drift toward it, but she doesn’t engage. She just watches the headlines slide by, like weather she can’t feel.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
I deserve to sit in this.
I deserve the weight.
I deserve the wine.

She picks up her phone. Opens her messages. Stares at **Scott’s name** in the contacts.

Thumb hovers.

Then retreats.

She sets it down screen-down, like it’s radioactive.

Another sip.

Then another.

She slides to the floor. Her back against the cabinet. Legs stretched out. Wine glass on her thigh. The roses in view. Still too red. Still too fresh.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
If I text him now…
it won’t be honest.
It’ll be wet and weak and guilt-colored.
He doesn’t deserve *that* version of me either.

She leans her head back against the cabinet.

Takes one final, deep sip.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
So I’ll just stay here.
In the middle of my trespass.
Until the bottle’s empty.
Or I am.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S KITCHEN – 8:03 P.M.**

**Sherry** is still on the floor. Hoodie bunched up around her elbows. Bare legs stretched across cold tile. The **wine bottle is almost gone**, glass sloshing in her hand like a warning bell.

The **TV glows quietly in the background**, still on mute.

She glances at it, eyes bleary. Just white noise.

Until—

**She sees it.**

The familiar **Tri-State Auto Center signage**, in shaky handheld live footage. A **local anchor** stands in front of the dealership, mic in hand, her breath visible in the cold night air.

**The chyron:**
**“LIVE: Owner of Local Dealership in ICU After Head-On Collision – Child Passenger in Critical Condition”**

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
…No.

She grabs the remote. Fumbles. **Unmutes.**

**ANCHOR (ON TV):**
—still awaiting official updates from Norton Children’s Hospital, where the minor passenger remains in critical condition tonight. Family friends say the boy’s father has been by his side since early Saturday morning.

The camera pans briefly to the lot. Police tape. A smashed SUV, just visible in the background.

Sherry’s wine glass slips from her hand. Hits the floor. Doesn’t break. Just spills.

She stares at the screen, breath held.

**ANCHOR (ON TV):**
We’re told the father, who has asked not to speak to the media at this time, was on scene shortly after the crash. Again, the condition of the child has not improved.

Sherry covers her mouth with both hands.

**SHERRY (V.O.)**
His kid.
His baby.
I thought he just… left.
I thought I was the one bleeding.

She pulls her knees into her chest. Tears don’t fall yet—they’re stuck behind shame. Behind *what she said*. What she *didn’t* say.

She reaches for her phone again.

Pulls up his contact.

Types:

> *I’m sorry.*

Backspaces.

Types:

> *I saw the news. I didn’t know. I didn’t—*

Backspaces again.

Closes the phone.

Leans back.

The roses are still on the counter.

Too red.
Too alive.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S LIVING ROOM – 11:52 P.M.**

The wine bottle is empty.

The TV is off now, screen black and reflective. The room is lit only by the **oven clock glowing green**: 11:52.

**Sherry** lies on the couch. Curled. Not asleep. Just… still.

She’s wrapped in a blanket, but **one arm remains outside**, reaching toward the mason jar with the roses. Her fingers brush the rim, like a tether.

The card sits face-down on the coffee table.

Her phone is next to it. No new notifications.

No missed calls.
No unread texts.
**No forgiveness looped back.**

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
He’s not texting back.
He’s in a hospital.
With his son.
Probably doesn’t even remember the version of me I’m trying to fix.

She stares at the ceiling.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
I don’t deserve an answer.
I just want one anyway.

A tear slips down her cheek. Slow. Quiet.

She doesn’t wipe it away.

The house creaks as the heat kicks on. Outside, a siren in the distance. Then nothing.

Just **silence**.

---

**INT. SHERRY’S BEDROOM – 3:17 A.M.**

She’s in bed now. Still in the hoodie. Still in the same position—facing away from her phone, though it’s on the pillow beside her.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
If I fall asleep, I won’t dream.
I’ll just coast for a few hours.
Then wake up guilty all over again.

The screen lights up briefly with a **calendar reminder**.

She ignores it.

Eyes open.

The clock glows on.

**Silence.**

---
---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OFFICE – WEDNESDAY, 9:14 A.M.**

**Sherry** sits at her desk. Fluorescent lights buzz. The coffee in her cup is *lukewarm at best*. She hasn’t touched it.

Her eyes are dull. Skin pale. No makeup today. Hair scraped back with zero effort.

**The roses are gone**—not thrown out, just not here.

Her inbox is full. Subject lines blur together. Budget approval. Student conflict. A request for an interdepartmental review.

She stares at it all like she’s reading a foreign language.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
I should be focused.
I should care about the numbers.
About the next meeting.
About anything that isn’t Saturday night.

A colleague knocks.

**COLLEAGUE (cheerfully):**
Hey, did you see the new semester rosters? We’ve got two whole sections waitlisted already.

**SHERRY (flat):**
That’s great.

**COLLEAGUE (awkward pause):**
You okay?

**SHERRY (manages a smile):**
Just tired.

They leave.

She opens a browser. Types **Norton Children’s Hospital, Cincinnati** into the search bar. Stops.

Backspaces.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
If he wanted me to know…
He’d tell me.

She reaches for her phone. Checks it.

Nothing.

**No missed calls.**
**No messages.**
**No updates.**

She sets it back down.

Checks the time: **9:17 A.M.**

It feels like noon.

---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OFFICE – 11:52 A.M.**

She’s made it through a staff meeting. Barely. Nodding when necessary. Pretending to take notes. She ate half a granola bar, more out of muscle memory than appetite.

She’s back at her desk now, eyes unfocused, watching the **cursor blink** in a blank Word doc.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
Maybe he’s sitting in a waiting room.
Maybe he’s crying.
Maybe he’s just trying to keep it together.

And I’m over here answering emails like my soul isn’t curled up under this desk.

---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OFFICE – 3:33 P.M.**

She opens **Cincinnati.com** again.

Refreshes the page.

Nothing new.

Same article. Same photo. Same words.

Still critical.

**Still silence.**

She closes the browser.

Just breathes.

And keeps going.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S KITCHEN – THURSDAY, 6:12 A.M.**

The sun hasn’t risen yet.

**Sherry** stands barefoot at the counter, wrapped in the same hoodie. A cup of coffee in one hand, staring through the kitchen window at *nothing*.

She didn’t sleep. Not really.

She went to bed.
She laid still.
She closed her eyes.
She waited for unconsciousness that never came.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
Forty-eight hours.
No real sleep.
No text.
No word.
Just the note.
And the silence that followed it.

She sips the coffee. It’s bitter. It hurts.

Good.

---

**INT. UNIVERSITY PARKING LOT – 7:29 A.M.**

She sits in her car. Still. Engine off. Hands gripping the wheel.

She’s wearing the same boots, a clean blouse, but no lipstick. Hair tied back in a messy twist.

Her phone is on the passenger seat.

She picks it up.

Still nothing.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
If I don’t hear from him today, I’ll stop hoping.
I have to.

She locks the phone. Leaves it in the car.

---

**INT. UNIVERSITY HALLWAY – 11:02 A.M.**

She walks down the corridor. Faculty pass her. Some smile. Some nod. She doesn’t register them.

She hears someone mention a car crash—**not his**, but just enough to make her body stiffen.

Everything is a trigger now.

Every sound, a possible update. Every silence, a verdict.

---

**INT. SHERRY’S OFFICE – 12:16 P.M.**

She’s reviewing a course evaluation spreadsheet. Her eyes flick over columns of numbers.

No retention.

She turns to her second monitor. Opens Cincinnati.com.

Refreshes.

**Nothing.**

No update. No headline. Not even a buried follow-up.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
If the kid dies, will I find out on the fucking website?

She slams her laptop shut.

Sits back.

The coffee’s gone cold again.

---

**INT. SHERRY’S BATHROOM – 3:41 P.M.**

She’s locked herself in the staff bathroom.

Sits on the closed toilet lid, head against the wall, eyes closed.

No crying.

Just the hum of the ventilation fan. The buzz of fluorescent lights. The heavy weight in her chest.

She opens her eyes and whispers to herself.

**SHERRY:**
I need this to end.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S OFFICE – THURSDAY, 4:12 P.M.**

She’s at her desk. Chair tilted back. Eyes closed.

Not sleeping. Not resting. Just… paused.

Her **phone buzzes** once on the desk.

**She jumps.**

Looks at it.

**iMESSAGE – from: Scott**
**[1 of 6]**

Her pulse skips.

She unlocks the phone.

The message thread unfolds in **gray and blue bubbles**, long and winding. Written quickly, but not carelessly.

---

> **SCOTT:**
> Hey.
>
> I know it’s been a few days.
>
> My son’s going to be okay. He had a lacerated spleen—internal bleeding, but they caught it early. No surgery, just bed rest, but it was touch-and-go for about 36 hours.
>
> He’s sleeping now. Finally. I think I am too, for the first time since Saturday.
>
> I didn’t mean to leave the way I did. I wanted to say something. You were in the bathroom. I panicked. I wrote a note, but… I figured you’d get it. I figured you’d understand. That was probably arrogant.
>
> I don’t blame you if you’re pissed. Or confused. Or just… done.
>
> But I didn’t vanish. I ran to my kid. And I’ve been there ever since.

---

Sherry stares at it. Reads it once. Again.

The words **"lacerated spleen"** loop in her brain like a siren.

She stands. Moves to the window. Phone still in hand.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
He didn’t owe me this.
But he sent it anyway.
After *everything.*

She types.

Stops.

Deletes.

Starts again.

**[TEXT – to: Scott]**
I’m so relieved he’s okay.
I’m so, so sorry I didn’t understand.
I wanted to. I just didn’t know.
I really didn’t know.

She hovers over **Send**.

Taps it.

Sets the phone down gently.

And finally… **lets herself cry**.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S OFFICE – THURSDAY, 4:36 P.M.**

Her eyes are red. Shoulders looser than they’ve been in days. She sits on the edge of her desk, holding her phone, waiting without knowing she’s waiting.

It pings again.

**iMESSAGE – from: Scott**
**[1 of 2]**

---

> **SCOTT:**
> I figured the flowers were a decent gesture.
> Didn’t want to just disappear after the mess.
> I thought I at least owed you something soft to balance how hard I had to come and go.
>
> Glad you got them.

---

Sherry reads it once.

Smiles—*just a little*. The phrasing is… bold. That last line, especially. But she reads through it.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
That’s Scott. Still rough around the edges. Still thinking he’s smoother than he is.
But he bought me flowers.
And he wrote that card.
And he let me sit in silence without pushing.

She walks to her office door, quietly locks it again.

Then replies:

---

> **SHERRY:**
> I got them.
>
> They were beautiful.
>
> You have a better instinct for grace than your wording sometimes suggests.
>
> But I’ll take both.

---

She hits **Send**.

Sets the phone down on the desk next to her coffee.

This time, she drinks it.

Warm. Steady.

---
---

**INT. SHERRY’S OFFICE – THURSDAY, 4:53 P.M.**

Her phone buzzes again. She’s just taken a sip of coffee, bracing herself for more information.

Instead:

**iMESSAGE – from: Scott**
**[1 of 3]**

---

> **SCOTT:**
> Also, not to make things complicated again…
>
> But I keep replaying you in those boots.
>
> And I’m not sure I’m going to recover from that anytime soon.

---

She exhales through her nose. Smiles. Rolls her eyes.

**SHERRY (V.O.):**
There it is.  The soft fade back into *Scott Mode.*

Her phone buzzes again:

---

> **SCOTT:**
> You were a hell of a thing that night.
>
> Even if the ending got away from me.
>
> I’ve got notes for myself too, by the way.
> Starting with “don’t bail on a gorgeous woman post-orgasm.”

---

She actually *laughs*. Quiet, but real.

Then types:

---

> **SHERRY:**
> Good note. You should bold that one. Maybe underline it twice.
>
> Also: boots are not responsible for emotional misfires. They are innocent bystanders.

Kathy Espich, known for fronting indie-rock band *Commuted*, was in Buenos Aires this week to raise funds and awareness for resistance movements fighting the spread of genetically modified crops.
