---

#### **SCENE: TEXTING ACROSS THE WORLD**

Sherry’s phone buzzes again.

It’s not the delay that surprises her—
**it’s the speed.**

He’s texting back **in real time**, just like before.

She checks the clock: **2:19 a.m.**

Then she remembers.

> *“He’s in Tokyo. It’s midafternoon there.”*

She can almost see it—Jeff, halfway around the world, maybe standing on a rooftop, maybe walking through Shibuya, holding that stupid overpriced phone, **laughing at something only he finds funny.**

And still… answering her.

Immediately.
Fully.
Like she matters.

It’s easier now.
She doesn’t have to whisper.
She doesn’t have to tiptoe.

> *“We’re not in the same place,”* she thinks,
> *“but we’re in the same moment.”*

She sends another message.

> *“What are you doing right now?”*

Three dots. They appear fast.

**[Jeff:]**
> *“Drinking a gin & tonic. Watching a guy try to walk five dogs at once.”*

> *“It’s 1,000 degrees. All the dogs are pissed.”*

She smiles.

---

#### **TEXT THREAD CONTINUES**

**[Sherry – 2:23 a.m.]**
> *“Who are they supposed to play?”*

**[Jeff – 3:25 p.m. Tokyo time]**
> *“Brewers. It’s gonna be messy. They’ve got that pitcher I hate. Big guy. Looks like he eats bricks.”*

**[Sherry – 2:24 a.m.]**
> *“So, a fight on Opening Day?”*

**[Jeff – 3:26 p.m.]**
> *“It’s Cincinnati. Opening Day *is* a fight.”*

**[Jeff – 3:27 p.m.]**
> *“God’s favorite civic holiday.”*

**[Sherry – 2:25 a.m.]**
> *“Remind me what I’m walking into?”*

**[Jeff – 3:28 p.m.]**
> *“Picture Mardi Gras. With more bratwurst. And everybody’s yelling about Dusty Baker.”*

**[Jeff – 3:29 p.m.]**
> *“You’ll love it. Or hate it. But either way, you’ll look amazing in red.”*

---

Ah, you came to the right place—**and you’re gonna love this**:

#### **Opening Day – March 31, 2011:**
**Cincinnati Reds vs. Milwaukee Brewers**
**Great American Ball Park**
**Result: Reds win 7–6 in a walk-off.**

And not just any walk-off.

**Ramon Hernandez hit a 3-run walk-off home run** in the bottom of the 9th to **win the game**, capping off a **4-run rally**.

The Reds were trailing 6–3 going into the bottom of the 9th.

- Brandon Phillips singled.
- Joey Votto walked.
- Scott Rolen hit an RBI single to make it 6–4.
- And then, **with two outs**, **Ramon Hernandez launched one over the left-field wall** for a three-run bomb.

**Stadium went absolutely nuclear.** **It was pure Cincinnati voodoo.**

#### So, in story terms?

Sherry’s first time walking back into Jeff’s world…Luxury suite… bandmates watching… emotions tangled…And the stadium **erupts in joy and chaos** as the Reds snatch victory **out of nowhere**.

**Symbolic much?** Hell yes. 

Want to weave that into the emotional climax of the day? Because that homer… that explosion… *that moment of crowd hysteria*…
It could very well mirror **something inside Sherry cracking wide open.**

---
You didn't plan it—But the **universe gave it to you anyway.**

A walk-off home run.  Bottom of the 9th.  Against the odds.  **Euphoria detonating in real time.**  

And there’s Sherry—

- Surrounded by the band, most of whom **don’t trust her.**
- Standing in a luxury suite she didn’t ask for.
- Wearing red because **Jeff told her to.**
- Watching the crowd around her go **absolutely primal.**
- With her own inner game in the 9th inning, **down by 3.**

**You couldn’t script it better.**  Now you’ve got **a stadium of 40,000 people screaming their lungs out**, and Sherry’s body responding with goosebumps—but it’s not the home run that hits her hardest.  It’s the moment **Jeff looks over at her and grins like he knew the ending all along.**

**Past performers:**
> *Michael Jackson, U2, Guns N’ Roses, Beyoncé, Madonna, The Rolling Stones, Taylor Swift.*

> *Jeff is… playing there?*

- **Bigger than Riverfront?** Yes.

**He dropped it like he was ordering coffee.**

She scrolls back to the list of performers.

#### **SCENE: SHERRY + YOUTUBE, CIRCA 2011**

It’s just after 3 a.m.

Laptop humming like a space heater.
Phone dimmed.
She’s got a tab open to YouTube—version **before streaming was sleek**, when comments were chaos and **videos took three minutes to buffer.**

She types:
> *commuted live*

The results load.  **Thousands. Not millions.**  But still too many to process. 

She scrolls.  Clicks one with a thumbnail from a **2008 show in Berlin**.
Title:
> *“COMMUTED LIVE — Germany — Kathy on FIRE!!!”*

The quality is garbage.
Audio clipped.
Shaky hands.
Phones in the crowd, but **barely anyone has a smartphone yet**.

And still—**there’s magic.**

Kathy’s center stage, barefoot, stalking the mic.
Her voice is **untamed thunder**, eyes closed like she’s holding back a vision.
The crowd? Frenzied.

Gilley struts stage right, hair covering half his face, looking like a **gothic preacher mid-exorcism**, throwing guitar stabs like he's casting spells.

And tucked way in the back left—

**Jeff.**

He’s still.
Effortless.
Shoulders barely moving.
Bass in his hands like it was born there.

The camera barely registers him.
But Sherry sees him.

The subtle shift when he cues the drummer.
The way he leans forward, ever so slightly, as Kathy launches into the bridge.
His backing mic goes live—his mouth moves—**but the fan with the camera doesn’t even bother to zoom in.**

She watches for five more minutes.
She watches like she’s reading between the lines.

> *“He was never the flame,”* she thinks.
> *“He was the oxygen.”*

She closes the tab.
Pulls the blanket over her knees.

And for the second time that night, she tells herself—

> *“I still picked Scott.”*

Only this time,
**she doesn’t say it like it’s the final word.**

---

#### **SCENE: SHERRY WATCHES, THINKS, Notices**

He had more hair back then.
Messy, loose around the ears.
It curled a little when he sweat.
She’d forgotten that.

Now, when she sees him—when they’ve video-chatted, when they’ve bumped into each other across years and silences—he keeps it short.
Cleaner. Sharper.
But somehow… **less alive.**

And yeah.
He’s gained weight.

Not a lot.
Not the kind that ruins a man.
But the kind that makes you realize he used to float across a stage and now he **moves with gravity**.
**Middle-age gravity.**

And his brother—Jeremy, right?

She squints at a side clip someone took from the wings.

Yep. That’s him.
Same jaw.
Same eyebrows.
**But a different build. Narrower. Leaner. Like a version of Jeff someone stretched just a little thinner.**

Jeremy looks like he still runs stairs for fun.
Jeff looks like he skips breakfast and still gains weight on coffee and bitterness.

And then—
**the singer.**

She stares.

**This guy.**

Gilley.

He’s on fire.
Not handsome in the traditional way, but **magnetic**.
He sings like he’s seducing the gods.
Shirt clinging, hair wild, eyes closed.

Even the camera wants him.
The crowd surges toward him like he’s a religious experience.
And when he drops his guitar between verses and leans into the mic—

> *“Jesus Christ.”*

Sherry blurts it aloud.
Catches herself.
Looks around the empty room.

She rewinds.

Watches Gilley move.

And the truth slaps her:

> *“This man might be the sexiest human on Earth.”*

But she’s not watching him, is she?

She’s watching Jeff.
In the corner.
**Outside the gravity well of the stage—but still tethered to it.**
Still playing like the world depends on his timing.

And it hits her:

> *“I never wanted the spotlight. I just wanted the one who built it.”*

The video’s grainy.

#### **SCENE: THE SELFIE**

Jeff. On stage.

Gigantic grin. Eyes lit up.

Like the weight he carries at home fell off at customs.

His shirt’s wrinkled, bass slung across his chest.
Cables trail at his feet.
There’s a technician in the background, blurry, fiddling with monitors.

**Jeff looks like he’s touching the sky.**

> *“This isn’t the man I’ve been fucking.”*

Not really.

Or—

> *“Did I just miss it because I never knew where to look?”*

Still lit.
Jeff’s smile glowing faintly on the lock screen.

Laptop fan still spinning.
Wine glass untouched.

Eyes like cotton.

She’s not ready for today.
But it’s coming anyway.

#### **SCENE: SHERRY TRIES TO TAKE THE DAY OFF**

**Wednesday, March 30, 2011 – 8:54 a.m.**
University admin building, third floor.

Sherry walks into the office with the kind of deliberate calm that **means she’s absolutely panicking inside.**
Hair tied back.
Laptop bag over one shoulder.
A folder under her arm **she doesn’t actually need**—prop only.

Rhonda’s sipping coffee from a novelty mug that says:
> *“I Excel At Excel”*

Without looking up, Rhonda says,
> “Whatever it is, Sherry, the answer is maybe.”

Sherry winces.

> “Hey, um… so I have a small favor to ask.”

**Rhonda looks up slowly.**
The way a cat does when it knows it’s going to win.

> “Is this about Opening Day?”

> “…Maybe.”

Rhonda leans back.
Taps one perfectly manicured fingernail on her desk.

> “Let me guess. You’re *suddenly overcome* with civic pride and just remembered the Reds exist?”

Sherry grins, sheepish.

> “I got a last-second invite. Luxury suite. Free food. It's kind of a thing.”

Rhonda arches an eyebrow.

> “Does this invite happen to be from a certain bass player who once had an autographed Def Leppard shirt delivered to *my mailroom*?”

Sherry groans.

> “That shirt was for me, not you.”

> “Oh I know,” Rhonda says, deadpan. “But the courier made quite a show of it. Had a clipboard. A tracking number. A fan club badge. The works.”

Sherry shrinks two inches into herself.

> “I’ll owe you one.”

> “You already owe me two.”

Beat.

> “…Please?”

Rhonda sips her coffee. Holds the silence like a violin string.

Then:
> “Fine. Go. But only if you wear that ridiculous red scarf that makes your hair look like a protest.”

Sherry beams.

> “Deal.”

Rhonda nods once.
Then, as Sherry turns to leave—

> “And Sherry?”

> “Yeah?”

> “If that man ever sends flowers to this office again, I’m keeping them.”

> “Fair.”

Not out of obligation.
Not out of kink.

**Out of intention.**

Her tongue flicks across the base of her palm—
one slow, deliberate sweep.

Then again—further up.
She licks along her fingers, tasting each trace.

**Salt.
Heat.
Something metallic.
Something else.
Something uniquely… Jeff.**

It’s not about the flavor.

It’s about the **mark**.
The **memory.**
The *unmistakable intimacy* of knowing him this way.

> *“Not brandy,”* she thinks.
> *“No… bourbon.
Something aged.
Complex.
Smoky in places I didn’t expect.”*

She pauses.
Tongue still gliding over her knuckle.

> *“I want to know this.
So next time—when it’s in my mouth,
when he gives me that—
I’ll know.
Without question.
That it’s him.
His gift.
To me.”*

She closes her eyes for one long second.

And savors.

---

#### **SCENE: 7:29**

The light is golden now—
not just the softness of morning,
but the *arrival* of it.

It washes across the sheets,
paints soft shadows on the wall,
warms the corners of the bed where their bodies do not touch.

Jeff is silent.
Breathing steady.
Eyes closed again—but not asleep.

Just… spent.
At peace.

Sherry sits upright beside him, her hand now clean,
but her lips still tasting of him.
Of surrender.
Of presence.
Of **clarity**.

She doesn’t check her phone.
Doesn’t reach for the covers.

She just sits.
Soaking in the moment.
The silence.
The knowledge.

**He came.
She received.
They met.
Right here.**

The clock on her dresser glows in pale digits:

**7:29.**

**And the day has only just begun.**

---

#### **SCENE: EVERYTHING**

Jeff’s voice is low.
Rough.
Still floating somewhere between sleep and awakening.

> “Jesus, Sherry…”
> “I didn’t treat you. I didn’t do anything for you.”

He doesn’t even open his eyes.
His words aren’t excuses.
Just regret.
The kind that comes from not knowing how to accept being cared for.

Sherry looks down at him.
The soft mess of his hair.
The mouth that kissed her yesterday.
The cock she just held in her hand,
now resting, quiet, **completely spent.**

And she says it simply.
Clearly.
With all the warmth in her heart—

> “You did everything for me.”

No smile.
No smirk.

Just truth.

---

#### **SCENE: TIME TO MOVE**

The silence hangs for just a second longer.

Jeff lies there—flat, half-awake, warm.
Still recovering.
Still wrapped in the aftermath of everything she gave him.

And then—

**Pat. Pat.**

Sherry’s hand lands twice on his bare hip.
Not soft.
Not hard.
Just firm enough to say: *get your ass moving.*

> “Come on, bud.”

Her voice is still low, but she’s switched gears now.
The cooing’s gone.
This is a woman who’s got a plan.

> “You gotta crank your ass into the shower…”

Jeff groans, barely lifting his head.

> “You got cum all over you,” she continues,
> “you smell like *ass*,
and you’ve got a lot of shit to do today.”

She stands up, grabs her robe, ties it in a practiced tug.

> “So unless you want to show up to Opening Day lookin’ like you rolled in from a meth convention,
get moving.”

Jeff groans again, dragging one arm over his face.

> “This is how you thank me?”

Sherry smirks over her shoulder as she walks to the bathroom.

> “Oh honey. That *was* the thank-you.”

---

#### **SCENE: DOMESTIC GODDESS, SHOWER EDITION**

Sherry opens the bathroom door, flips on the light, and starts the shower with a practiced twist of the knob.
It’s not fancy.
No spa fixtures.
No waterfall.

Just **water.
Heat.
Function.**

And it works.

Jeff stumbles in behind her, still blinking like someone who’s been born again into a new, semi-lubricated world.

She gives him a once-over.

> “Christ, you look like a war orphan.”

He shrugs, steps into the shower, and lets the stream hit him straight in the chest.

Steam starts to fill the small space.

> “Don’t mind me,” he mumbles, eyes half-shut,
> “I’m just going to stand here under the water and pretend I’m still asleep.”

Sherry snorts, crosses her arms, and leans against the doorframe.

> “This ain’t Tokyo, Rock Star.
No twenty-foot ceilings.
No ten-head rainforest deluge system.
This is Kentucky.
You’re under a suburban water heater that holds exactly one tank’s worth of hot.
So you got fifteen minutes before you’re shivering like a wet Chihuahua.”

Jeff lifts a hand weakly, offers a thumbs-up without opening his eyes.

> “Noted.”

She rolls her eyes—
but there’s a smile tugging at the corners of her mouth.

> *“He’s home.”*

---

#### **SCENE: WATER WON’T WIN**

The bathroom is thick with steam.
Sherry steps in behind him, careful on the tile.
The water’s warm—just right.

Jeff doesn’t move.
He’s standing dead-center in the stream,
his head bowed,
water pouring over him like he’s trying to let it baptize him out of jet lag and overexertion.

But it’s **not working.**

His arms hang at his sides.
His hair flattened to his skull.
His breath is steady, slow, like he could fall asleep right there.

Sherry steps closer, just behind him.
The water hits her shoulders, streams down her back.

She doesn’t say anything at first.
Just stands there with him, sharing the heat.

Then, softly—

> “You look like you’re trying to fight the water and lose.”

Jeff doesn’t lift his head.

> “I am.”
> “So far the water is winning by attrition.”

She watches a single droplet curve along his spine.
Then she reaches out, runs her hand gently across his lower back, up to his shoulder blade.

> “You gonna make it through Opening Day, old man?”

A grunt.

> “If they carry me.”

Sherry leans in, rests her forehead between his shoulder blades.

> “Then I’ll carry you.”

He stands there, still letting the water pour down.
Still not moving.

But he nods.

**Once.**

Quiet.
Simple.
Honest.

---
#### **SCENE: THE WASHBASIN CONFESSION**

The water keeps falling, steady and hot.

Jeff finally shifts just slightly, tilts his head forward under the spray, and speaks—

> “If you want…
you can wash my hair.”

Sherry blinks.

> “Are you goofing on me?”

He doesn’t even lift his head.
His voice stays low, half in the water, half in the steam.

> “Nope.”
> “Not fooling.
Not trying to be cute.
I’m just that tired.
Right now I don’t want to lift my hands above my shoulders.”

There’s no shame in his voice.
No flirtation.
Just honesty.
**Just need.**

Sherry watches him for a moment.
Then slowly reaches for the shampoo.
A small bottle. Nothing fancy.

She squeezes a dollop into her palm, works it into a gentle lather between her hands.

> “Alright, rockstar,” she murmurs, stepping closer.
> “Let’s get you sorted.”

She presses her fingers into his scalp, slow and firm.
His hair slicks under her hands.
She starts to massage—circular motion, steady rhythm.

He exhales.
**Deep. Grateful. Almost wordless.**

> “Oh my God,” he murmurs, voice almost breaking,
> “that’s… actually doing something.”

Sherry grins.

> “Welcome to spa day, dumbass.”

---

#### **SCENE: SUDS AND SARCASM, CLEAN TAKE**

Sherry finishes rinsing the shampoo from Jeff’s hair, watching it run in soapy streams over his neck and down his back. He hasn’t moved much, aside from sighing like a man in a coma who's found religion.

Then—he finally stirs.

> “Alright, moment of truth—”
> “Do you have any *man soap* in this house, or am I about to walk into Opening Day smelling like fruit salad and sparkles?”

Sherry lifts the loofah and stares at him like he just personally insulted her tax bracket.

> “You afraid of being delicious?”

Jeff gives a lazy shrug under the water.

> “I’m afraid of smelling like I fell into the clearance bin at a glitter-themed bath boutique.”

She squeezes a thick ribbon of body wash onto the loofah, working it into a dense lather.

> “Relax. This one’s coconut and cedar.”

Jeff squints.

> “Coconut’s cutting it close.”

> “It’s got *cedar* in it. Trees. Bark. Outdoorsy man stuff.”

He grunts in acceptance.

> “Alright. Wood-scented fruit. I’ll allow it.”

She presses the loofah to his shoulder and begins to scrub—slow, steady.

> “You’re lucky I didn’t hit you with vanilla sugar and moonlight.”

Jeff exhales through a smirk.

> “You’re lucky I didn’t bring my backup bar of soap with wolf howls on the label and a warning for flammability.”

> “Mmm. Alpha soap. That your cologne too?”

> “Only when I need to win a knife fight in the woods.”

> “Don’t tempt me.”

---
#### **SCENE: SCENT OF A MAN**

Sherry drags the loofah across his chest now, slow and methodical, while Jeff leans slightly against the tile wall like he’s hanging onto the last bit of gravity.

> “You know,” he mutters,
> “the only cologne I’ve ever worn in my life comes from Degree Antiperspirant.”

She pauses, raises one eyebrow, but keeps scrubbing.

> “That explains so much.”

He gestures vaguely in the steam.

> “It’s called *Victory.* It’s supposed to last seventy-two hours.”

She leans in, mock-intrigued.

> “Does it?”

He snorts.

> “Nope.
Absolute bullshit.
I get six hours, maybe seven, and that’s if I don’t do anything more intense than stand upright and breathe.”

> “So… marketing lies?”

> “Nah,” he says, eyes half-lidded under the spray.
> “Just my body rejecting the notion of being contained by deodorant. I sweat like a Viking.”

Sherry gives his underarm a pointed look, then goes back to scrubbing his back.

> “You smell like victory, alright.
A very damp, *jet-lagged*, barely-standing kind of victory.”

He grins without opening his eyes.

> “The best kind.”

---

#### **SCENE: THE LAST OF THE STEAM**

Sherry steps out, careful not to slip on the slick tile.
She grabs her towel, wraps it tight around her torso, and starts patting herself dry.

Behind her, the water still runs.

Jeff lowers himself into the tub—legs stretched out, head tilted back into the spray like it’s a second attempt at resurrection.

> “You ever try to sleep on a plane for thirteen hours?”

Sherry glances back.

> “Nope. Closest I’ve come is falling asleep on a Greyhound next to a man eating hard-boiled eggs.”

Jeff groans.

> “Same vibe. But louder. More metal. And the seats? They lie to you.”

Sherry raises an eyebrow, toweling off her arms.

> “How can a seat lie?”

> “Because they say they *recline.* But it’s not a recline.
It’s a *shame angle.*
It tilts back like… three degrees.
Just enough to give you false hope and back pain.”

Sherry grabs her robe off the hook, starts slipping it on.

> “And the food?”

> “Plastic box full of damp dreams and sadness.”

She chuckles.

> “You poor thing.”

Jeff doesn't open his eyes—he just lets the water hit his chest one last time.

> “It’s like they trap your soul somewhere over the Pacific and make you pay three hundred dollars for a gin and tonic while you watch a dubbed version of *Fast & Furious 8* and question your life choices.”

Sherry ties her robe and leans in the doorway.

> “Sounds like you had a blast.”

> “Oh, I did,” he says, voice muffled by steam.
> “I’m a broken man.”

She tosses him a towel.

> “Then dry off, broken man.
We’ve got baseball and bourbon in your near future.”

---

#### **SCENE: THE MANIFESTO**

Jeff’s still in the tub, head back, eyes closed, water dripping off his jaw.
He sounds like a man testifying in front of Congress.

> “I’m never doing this again.”

Sherry, now fully robed and working a towel through her hair, gives him a side glance.

> “Doing what? Traveling the world? Being a rock god? Getting off before sunrise?”

He waves one arm, limp and dramatic.

> “Flying commercial.
First class is a goddamn lie.”

> “Pretty sure it’s still better than economy.”

> “It’s just economy with a slightly bigger tray table and a curtain of shame.
The seats look fancy but they were designed by ex-Stasi agents.
They recline just enough to paralyze your spine in six different ways.”

Sherry leans in the doorway, eyebrow raised.

> “So what’s the plan, Mr. Rockstar?”

Jeff opens one eye.

> “Fractional jet share.”

> “You serious?”

> “Deadly.
I’ve made it.
By God, I’ve **earned** the right to not be folded like a lawn chair over the Pacific ever again.”

He sits up now, water sloshing.

> “I want to stretch out. I want to sleep like a human.
I want a blanket that doesn't feel like a recycled trash bag.
And maybe… just maybe… have room to do more than sleep.”

Sherry crosses her arms.

> “Define *more.*”

Jeff grins, wicked and sleepy.

> “I’ll let you decide that, once we’re at cruising altitude.”

She shakes her head, laughing softly.

> “Well then, Captain Fancy Pants, dry off.
We’ve got hot dogs and Opening Day miracles to attend.”

---

#### **SCENE: THE GULF**

Sherry stands in the doorway, watching him towel off like a half-drowned golden retriever, ranting about jet shares and the ergonomics of luxury misery.

She doesn’t say anything for a second.

Because her brain’s already gone somewhere else.

> *When she went to Hawaii…*

Middle seat.
Back of the plane.
Twelve hours of cramped knees, recycled air, a kid screaming three rows up.

No sleep.
No glass of champagne waiting on boarding.
No **lie-flat seat.**
No idea that the world could even offer anything different.

She didn’t complain.
She’d saved for that trip for **three years.**
It was **worth every cramp.**

But still—

Here he is.
Fresh off Tokyo,
bitching about first class
like it was a war crime.

> *Jesus Christ.*

It’s not resentment.
Not yet.

But it is a reminder.

Of the **difference**.
The **gap.**
The **magnitude of their lives**,
and how easily he floats across it—
while she’s spent decades crawling up the incline.

She watches him for a beat longer, then clears her throat and says—

> “Well, some of us don’t mind being folded like a lawn chair.
We just call that *vacation.*”

Jeff looks up, blinking.

> “Huh?”

She forces a smile.

> “Never mind. Let’s get dressed.”

---

#### **SCENE: A GULFSTREAM AWAY**

Jeff pulls the towel around his waist, still dripping, still flushed from the heat of the water and whatever endorphins he has left in the tank.

> “You know,” he says casually, running a hand through his wet hair,
> “if I did one of those jet shares, I could get a bed. Not a full king or anything, but enough. One that fits two.”

He glances at her. His eyes are playful, earnest.

> “Gulfstreams don’t have to be that big. But they go real far.
We could make it to Tahiti in one hop.
As long as you leave from the west coast.”

Sherry freezes for a second.

Not visibly.
Not with drama.
But just… *internally*.

She wraps her robe a little tighter.

> *“We.”*

> *“Tahiti.”*

> *“In one hop.”*

And she’s right back to that flight to Hawaii.
Economy.
Two layovers.
Bag of peanuts.
Gate change in Dallas that made her run like hell in flip-flops.

Jeff is talking about **private jets** like she talks about choosing gas stations.

He’s not bragging.
He’s just imagining.
Including her, even.

But the **gap feels louder** now.

She doesn’t answer right away.

Just nods, half-smiling, half-somewhere else.

> “Maybe someday,” she says.

Jeff grins.

> “Yeah. Someday.”

She nods, pulling a shirt over her head.

It’s not biting.

Reflective.

You always notice.

> “Shit, Sherry.
I didn’t mean to miss that.
I just—I wasn’t even in my own body last night.
That flight chewed me up and spit me out.
You could’ve walked in wearing tassels and carrying bourbon and I still would've barely registered it.”

Sherry smiles.
Warm. Understanding.

> “I figured.
I just wanted to make sure you were… back.”

He steps toward her, wraps his arms around her towel-damp and all.

> “I’m back.”

A beat.

> “But next time you leave the bra at home, give me a heads-up.
I’ll schedule the parade.”

She laughs into his shoulder, the tension dissolving into steam.

#### **SCENE: MORNING ORDERS**

Jeff leans against the doorway, towel loose around his hips, hair dripping, eyes half-lidded like a man surviving the Battle of Jet Lag.

He lifts a finger. A declaration. A desperate prayer.

> “I need two things, Sherry.”

Sherry, halfway through putting on her boot, pauses.

> “That’s already more than two.”

He ignores her.

> “I need coffee.
I need Mountain Dew.
I need Excedrin Migraine.
And I need breakfast.”

She squints at him.

> “You just listed four.”

> “They’re emotionally grouped into two categories.
One’s for waking up.
The other’s to make me believe life is worth waking up to.”

She smirks, grabs her keys off the dresser.

> “Alright, genius.
Coffee’s on deck.
I’ve got a cold Dew in the fridge.
Excedrin’s in the top drawer.
And if you want breakfast, your ass better be dressed in five minutes or I’m ordering Waffle House for one.”

> “You already did.
You forgot I wasn’t wearing a bra.”

> “That wasn’t betrayal.
That was medically-induced blindness.”

> “Mm-hmm.”

She tosses him a clean pair of boxers and heads down the hall.

> “You’ve got four minutes.”

Jeff grins, rubbing the towel across his face like a war veteran preparing for the next skirmish.

> “I love this woman.”
