#### **SCENE: THE MEDICINE AND THE MATH**

Jeff tears open the foil packet of Excedrin like he’s defusing a bomb with a hangover.
One bright white tablet rolls onto the counter. He stares at it like it owes him money.

> “Alright, little buddy.
Do your thing.”

He pops it into his mouth and immediately chases it with a long, icy swig of Mountain Dew. The fizz hits his throat like a caffeinated gut punch, but he doesn’t flinch.
This is ritual.

Sherry watches him from the kitchen table, nursing her coffee.

> “You okay?”

He wipes his mouth with the back of his hand and leans against the counter, still half-dressed.

> “Yeah. I’ll be better in an hour or so.
Once the caffeine kicks in and the pharmaceutical angels start playing the harp in my skull.”

She raises an eyebrow.

> “Quite the lifestyle.”

Jeff smirks, but there’s a tug at the edge of it.

> “I love it.
I love rock.
I love the *whole shebang*—sex, drugs, and rock and roll.”

He leans forward, both palms on the counter, voice dropping an octave.

> “But it’s a young man’s game.
And I’m no longer *young*.”

Sherry sips her coffee.

> “But you're still playing it.”

Jeff shrugs.

> “Yeah.
But I need a better trainer.
And maybe a second liver.”

They both chuckle.

Then, silence.

Just two people at the start of a very long day—each bringing something bruised and something burning.

---

#### **SCENE: ROAD TO WAFFLE HOUSE**

The SUV rumbles to life.
Sherry adjusts her mirrors, pops the gear into reverse, and gently eases out of the driveway.

Jeff’s in the passenger seat, sunglasses on, slouched with Mountain Dew in hand, tapping the bottom of the bottle like it owes him rent.

Sherry steals a glance.

> “You good?”

He grunts affirmatively, eyes closed behind the lenses.

She waits a beat.
Then speaks—casual, but calibrated.

> “So… can I ask you something?”

> “You just did.”

> “Funny.”

He tilts his head toward her.

> “Shoot.”

> “What’s your philosophy on exclusivity?
You know—when it comes to… *this.*”

She gestures between them, eyes on the road.

Jeff sits up slightly, bottle still in his hand.

> “You mean… like monogamy?”

> “Yeah.
Not asking for anything right this second, but I need to know how you roll.
Some people assume.
Some people negotiate.
Some people don’t care.
I just… don’t like surprises.”

Jeff doesn’t answer right away.
He’s thinking.

> “Well…
I think people should say what they want.
If you want exclusivity, say it.
If you don’t, say that too.
No gray area. No guessing.”

Sherry nods.

> “So you’re not against it?”

> “Not at all.
But I need a conversation.
Not just assumptions and landmines.”

She exhales. Not relief, not tension.
Just a measured breath.

> “Good.
Because last time I did gray area, I got a pile of regrets and a ruined carpet.”

Jeff chuckles.

> “That sounds like a hell of a story.”

> “One for another Waffle House run.”

He grins, slumps back in his seat.

> “Alright.
If it ever gets serious, I’ll bring a notary.”

> “Just bring honesty.”

They drive in silence for a few seconds.

The golden panels of a Waffle House appear in the distance like a holy beacon.

---

#### **SCENE: WARM CABIN, COOL AIR**

The SUV hums down the back road toward Waffle House, sunlight spilling across the dash.

Sherry keeps one hand on the wheel, eyes steady, her voice clear—not raised, not rattled.

> “Listen, Jeff.”

He turns slightly in his seat.

> “Yeah?”

She keeps her gaze on the road.

> “I’m a grown-ass woman.
I’ve lived through enough bullshit to know what I want.
And what I want… is to be treated like I matter.”

He doesn’t interrupt.

> “Not just as someone warm to wake up next to.
Not just someone who makes you laugh, or who’ll go down on you when you’re wrecked from a flight.”

She glances over.

> “I want to be treated like I’m **special**.
Like I’m someone you see when you look past the noise.
A soul partner, if you catch my drift.”

Jeff exhales—slow, audible, but says nothing yet.

She continues.

> “Doesn’t have to mean wedding bells or shared tax returns.
But if this… *thing* between us is going anywhere,
I need to know it’s being built on something more than just chemistry and nostalgia.”

A pause.

The road ahead widens. The Waffle House sign appears just over the crest.

She taps the brakes gently and adds, with a smile:

> “That make sense, Rockstar?”

---
#### **SCENE: AT THE STOPLIGHT, QUESTIONS THAT MATTER**

They’re stopped at a red light, the golden Waffle House sign glowing like a neon sermon ahead.

Sherry glances over, expression level.

> “Do I get a pass outside of the continental United States of America or not?”

Jeff looks at her, eyebrows raised just a hair.

She doesn’t blink.

> “Because that’s important.
I just want to know where I stand.”

He sits back, bottle of Mountain Dew balanced loosely between his fingers, and you can almost see the gears turn behind his eyes.

No defensiveness.
No slick answers.

Just the weight of the question settling in his lap.

> “You’re asking,” he says slowly, “if geography changes loyalty?”

> “I’m asking,” she replies, “if your zipper’s on a customs exemption.”

A beat.

He exhales through his nose.
Soft laugh. Not mockery. Just realization.

> “Fair question.”

She waits.

> “No,” he says. “You don’t get a pass. Not even in Guam.
If we say this is *us*—then it’s **us.** Wherever we are.”

A pause.

> “That’s the rule I want too.”

Sherry gives a small nod, lips pressed together.
Not giddy. Not glowing.

Just **seen.**

She eases the SUV forward into the parking lot.

> “Alright then. Let’s get waffles.”

---

#### **SCENE: TABLE #7, WAFFLE HOUSE**

The waitress drops off their plates—
three orders of sausage, one giant golden waffle, butter melting into its crevices like sunlight on Sunday.

Jeff grabs a fork and knife like he’s about to carve a Thanksgiving turkey.
But before he digs in, he holds up a finger.

> “Hey.
This part’s important.
You’ve got to really pay attention to this part.”

Sherry looks up mid-syrup-pour.

> “Okay…”

> “No, seriously. Swear to me.
Swear on your favorite boots.”

She raises an eyebrow, amused.

> “Alright, fine. I swear.”

Jeff lowers his voice like he’s about to share nuclear launch codes.

> “Do *not* let me eat chocolate and sausage on the same day.
Ever.”

Sherry blinks.

> “What?”

> “Chocolate.
And sausage.
**Same day.**
Migraine. Biblical. Brain tries to tunnel out of my skull.
Feels like a car crash in slow motion.
One time I did it at Bonnaroo and I thought I met God.
Turned out it was just the medic giving me Gatorade.”

Sherry stares.

> “That’s the dumbest-sounding rule I’ve ever heard.”

> “And yet, now it’s your sacred duty.
You’re my… dietary bodyguard.”

She takes a bite of waffle, chewing slowly.

> “Alright. No chocolate. No sausage. Same day. Got it.
But just to be clear—today’s only sausage, right?”

Jeff lifts his fork like a solemn oath.

> “Blessed be this pork. And nothing else.”

---

#### **SCENE: BITTERSWEET AND SAUSAGE**

Jeff cuts into the last of his waffle, wiping up syrup with a chunk of sausage.

> “You know how we figured out the migraine thing?”

Sherry looks up.

> “I assumed chaos, tears, and someone yelling ‘Ibuprofen!’”

Jeff smiles, but it fades into something softer.

> “My ex-wife tracked everything I ate for nearly a year.
Every snack. Every ingredient.
She had a notebook—hell, *notebooks*—color-coded, timestamped.
Like a damn scientist.”

He sets the fork down, more contemplative than before.

> “We thought it was stress, dehydration, barometric pressure…
Turned out to be *chocolate and sausage* in a 24-hour window.
Go figure.”

Sherry nods slowly, not interrupting.

> “She did that for you?”

> “Yeah.
That was one of her better chapters.
I’ll give her that.”

He leans back in the booth, gaze drifting slightly to the window.

> “My kids are the only thing I really got out of that marriage.
Them, and the knowledge that Hershey’s Kisses and breakfast sausage are a war crime against my brain.”

A beat.
A breath.

Then, with a wry smirk:

> “But I still miss the notebooks.
Nobody’s been that organized about me since.”

Sherry smiles across the table, warm and knowing.

> “You’re not that hard to read, Rockstar.
You just come with footnotes.”

Jeff chuckles, shaking his head.

> “Maybe so.
But I’ve learned to appreciate anyone who reads all the way through.”

---
#### **SCENE: SHARED WEIGHTS, UNEVEN TABLES**

Jeff leans back in the booth, eyes soft with memory.

Sherry sips her coffee, then reaches down into her bag.
Pulls out a thin, battered spiral-bound booklet.
Sets it next to her plate.

> “I can relate.”

Jeff looks over.

> “What’s that?”

> “Carb counter.
I carry it everywhere.
I can tell you how many grams are in just about anything at this place.”

She flips it open, thumb brushing dog-eared pages like she’s done it a thousand times—because she has.

> “My son’s with his dad today. At school.
Or trying to play hooky and charm the substitute teacher.
But every meal, every snack, every sip of juice—it’s a calculation.”

She doesn’t say it dramatically.
She says it like someone who’s built a second brain just to **keep her child alive.**

> “Because if I mess up?
It’s not a headache.
It’s an ambulance.”

Jeff nods slowly, watching her—not the book.

> “That’s a hell of a responsibility.”

She shrugs lightly, but not dismissively.

> “It’s just life.
You learn to carry it.”

A beat.

She offers a small smile.

> “So yeah… I get what it’s like to live by rules.
Even the dumb ones.
Especially the dumb ones.”

Jeff’s grin returns, slower this time.

> “Chocolate and sausage still sounds worse than insulin math.”

> “Try raising a teenager with a glucose monitor in his backpack.”

They both laugh—light, but grounded.
Not because anything’s funny.
Because they’ve both *survived something.*

And in that quiet moment over half-drunk coffee and cooling waffles, they don’t feel quite so alone.

---

#### **SCENE: BITTERSWEET REALITY**

Sherry’s thumb lingers on the page of her carb booklet.
Her coffee’s gone cold, but she doesn’t notice.

She looks up at Jeff—not accusing, not asking anything.
Just sharing.

> “Did you know…
a grown man—*after sex*—is supposed to test his blood sugar?”

Jeff blinks, caught off guard.

> “Wait. What?”

She nods, lips pressed into a faint, resigned smile.

> “Yeah.
Because the effort, the energy burn… the adrenaline, the release—
it can send you into a crash.
So, after he… you know…”

She trails off.

Jeff, gently:

> “Spills out?”

> “Yeah.
He’s supposed to check.
Prick his finger. Run the numbers.
Make sure he doesn’t pass out or worse.”

She folds the booklet closed with a quiet snap.

> “Isn’t that the saddest thing you’ve ever heard?”

Jeff’s face is unreadable—caught somewhere between heartbreak and awe.

> “Jesus.”

Sherry shrugs, eyes a little distant now.

> “It’s his normal.
It’s our normal.”

A pause. A breath.

> “Doesn’t stop him from flirting, though.
Little shit has charm for days.”

Jeff lets out a quiet chuckle, but it fades fast.

He looks at her, serious now.

> “You’re doing one hell of a job.”

Sherry looks down at her plate.

> “I try.
Some days that’s all I can do.”

And for a second, there’s no waitress, no clinking silverware, no jukebox humming in the background.

Just two people who’ve both carried more than their share of the weight—
And found each other at a booth in a Waffle House
**with eyes that understand.**

---

#### **SCENE: RETURN TO EARTH, SAUSAGE-LEVEL**

The silence hovers.

A quiet, heavy moment between them.

Then Jeff leans forward, one eyebrow raised, eyes flicking toward her plate.

> “Are you gonna eat your sausage, Sherry?”

She blinks—snapped out of the depths—
Then lets out a breath that’s half a laugh, half a sigh.

> “Seriously?”

> “What? I’m doing you a favor. It’s a migraine trigger. Remember? I’m a *responsible adult* now.”

Sherry side-eyes him, mock-suspicious.

> “You just want my food.”

> “That’s how it starts. Next thing you know, I’ve moved in, claimed drawer space, and reorganized your fridge.”

She slides the plate slightly toward him.

> “Fine. But don’t act like I’m not watching for chocolate, too.”

Jeff salutes her with a fork.

> “Noted. No dessert orgies. Just pork-based thievery.”

They both smile.
Lighter now.

Still carrying what they carry—
but doing it **together.**

---

#### **SCENE: FROM WAFFLES TO THE STADIUM**

Sherry pulls the SUV back onto the main road, slipping into the morning flow of traffic.
Downtown Cincinnati is already pulsing—
spring sun, ballpark energy, and the unmistakable buzz of Opening Day.

She glances at the clock on the dashboard.

> “We’re not catching the parade.”

Jeff shrugs from the passenger seat, sipping the last of his Mountain Dew like it’s holy water.

> “Too bad.
It’s awesome. Like Mardi Gras with more baseball and less beads.
But… here.”

He reaches into his backpack, pulls out a sleek black envelope, and hands her a card.

> “Garage pass. Address is on the back.
It’s under the stadium. Private access. Just follow the signs, flash the badge, and don’t run over any ushers.”

She flips it over, reading it with one eyebrow raised.

> “This feels very… *not Sherry.*”

> “That’s okay. It’s *me.*
And today, you’re rolling with me.”

She gives him a look—half teasing, half wary.

> “So what, we’ll be the first ones there?”

> “Probably.
Kathy’s never on time. Jeremy gets lost even with GPS.
Gilley usually needs to argue with a parking attendant about ‘artistic freedom.’
So yeah…
You and me. We’ll be the hosts.”

Sherry smirks, navigating onto the interstate ramp.

> “Great. I’ll pass out name tags.
Hi, I’m Jeff’s exhausted, underfed, sausage-less date.”

Jeff laughs.

> “And I’ll be the guy who looks like he slept in a ditch behind a Tokyo karaoke bar.”

The skyline appears ahead—
sunlight glinting off glass towers, the tip of the stadium just coming into view.

For a moment, Sherry doesn’t say anything.
Just drives.
Just breathes.
Just lets it all rise around her—like steam off a fresh cup of coffee.

---

#### **SCENE: INTERSTATE FLIRTATION, PARTIAL DISCLOSURE**

Jeff sits up a little straighter in the passenger seat, rubbing his eyes, stretching his arms.

The caffeine’s landed.
The migraine’s retreated.
The world’s in focus again.

He watches the city inch closer through the windshield, then glances sideways with a sly grin.

> “You ever been to New Orleans? Mardi Gras?”

Sherry shakes her head.

> “Nope. Closest I’ve gotten is Bourbon chicken from a mall food court.”

Jeff chuckles.

> “Would you flash your tits?”

She snorts.

> “That’s subtle.”

> “Hey, I’m just taking the cultural temperature of my passenger.
It’s research. Anthropological.”

She smirks, eyes still on the road.

> “If it was New Orleans,
if it was late at night,
and it was *actually* Mardi Gras…”

A beat. She shrugs.

> “Yeah. I probably would.”

Jeff grins, leans his head against the seat.

> “Good to know.
Mental image acquired.”

Sherry laughs.

> “You’re not even subtle about it.”

> “I haven’t been subtle since the Clinton administration.”

They drive on in silence for a few seconds.

And then Jeff, softer now:

> “Just seems like the kind of moment where a person feels free.
Like the rules don’t apply.
Just joy. Just being.”

Sherry glances over at him.

> “Maybe we both need a little more of that.”

He nods.

> “Maybe we do.”

---

#### **SCENE: THE RIVERFRONT GAUNTLET**

They roll into downtown—
and the temperature, the *pressure* of the city, spikes immediately.

Cincinnati Police officers in bright yellow windbreakers are stationed at **every** intersection, every garage, every barricade.
Whistles.
Flashlights.
Shouted directions cutting through the car horns and scattered chants of *Let’s go Reds!*

Jeff cracks his window an inch.

> “This is when it turns from baseball to religion.”

Sherry eases the SUV forward, following hand signals from a cop with a clipboard and mirrored sunglasses.

> “This is nuts.”

> “It’s always like this.
Opening Day in Cincinnati is like Christmas, Easter, and the second coming all wrapped in a ballgame.”

She laughs, inching toward the entrance to the stadium garage.

> “Where do I go?”

Jeff reaches over, taps the dash.

> “Badge. Hold it up.”

She does.
Instant shift in body language from the officer nearby—hand out, waving them forward with a sharp nod.

They’re in.

Descending into the concrete spiral of the private garage, past a sign marked:

**TEAM & VIP ONLY — NO PUBLIC ACCESS**

Jeff exhales slowly, rubbing the back of his neck.

> “And just like that, we’re behind the curtain.”

Sherry eases into a space labeled **Suite Level Reserved**, kills the engine, and looks around.

It’s quiet here.
Oddly serene.
Just the low hum of infrastructure and the faint thump of a marching band somewhere blocks away.

She glances over at Jeff.

> “Now what?”

Jeff grins and unbuckles.

> “Now we go play host to the weirdest family reunion on Earth.”

---

#### **SCENE: GEARING UP FOR THE BIG SHOW**

In the still hush of the garage, Jeff swings his backpack onto one shoulder, rummaging briefly before pulling out two caps.

One—sun-faded, beat to hell, threadbare like a war veteran.
The classic red wishbone C, dulled to a quiet maroon.

“This one’s mine.
Sixteen years old.
I think it’s technically a biohazard now.”

Sherry raises an eyebrow as he plops it on his head like a crown.

> “Smells like victory?”

> “Smells like beer, sweat, and three playoff heartbreaks. But yeah—*victory.*”

Then he turns, holding out the other cap.
Soft pink.
Crisp white wishbone C.
Brand new, tags barely snipped.

> “Figured if we’re showing up as a pair, you should have your own halo.”

Sherry takes it gently, almost surprised. She looks at it like it’s breakable.

> “It’s really cute.”

> “Don’t say that.
It’s *cool.*
It’s fierce. It’s suite-worthy.”

She snorts.

> “So I get a hot dog too?”

Jeff just stares at her, mock-offended.

> “Sherry.
We’re about to walk into a suite with an open bar, a sushi station, charcuterie, bison sliders, and a woman named Carla who *will* offer you a bourbon that costs more than your jeans.”

She grins.

> “So… yes?”

> “You can have five.
They’re all-beef. Kosher. Probably blessed by three rabbis and the ghost of Johnny Bench.”

She puts on the cap and flips the visor up slightly.

> “In that case…
I’ll take mine with mustard. And no guilt.”

Jeff taps the brim of her hat like he’s tipping it.

> “That’s the spirit.”

They head toward the elevator—two figures stepping out of the concrete shadow and into the glow of Opening Day.

---
---
---

#### **SCENE: ELEVATOR CONVERSATION — RESPECT TO A LEGEND**

Jeff adjusts the brim of his ancient Reds cap as the elevator hums upward.

> “You know what the best part of today is?”

Sherry glances his way.

> “The meat buffet? The private bathroom? The pink hat you just gave me that already feels like a personality trait?”

Jeff laughs, shakes his head.

> “Nah.
It’s that I’m in a room where nobody gives a damn who I am.
There are people up there who make *me* feel like a teenager.”

He grins.

> “I saw Barry Larkin in this suite two years ago.
*Barry freakin’ Larkin.*
You think anyone cares about a guy who plays bass when *that* man walks in?”

Sherry blinks.

> “He was here?”

> “He’s always here.
He *is* Opening Day.
There’s a bronze version of him two floors down.”

Jeff chuckles, then softens a bit.

> “I love it.
I get to be invisible.
Just a fan with a seat, a hot dog, and someone worth showing off.”

The elevator chimes.
Doors part to a hallway rich with quiet elegance and Reds memorabilia.
The pulse of the stadium is muffled here, sacred.

Jeff turns to her, a hand on the door.

> “Let’s go be nobodies in a room full of legends.”

Sherry smiles, hat squared and proud.

> “Hell yes.”

---
---

#### **SCENE: ENTERING THE SUITE — BACKSTAGE TO THE CITY**

The door swings open with a discreet *click*.

The room is bright—**all glass and gleam**, floor-to-ceiling windows looking out onto the ballpark, light pouring in across sleek furniture and crisp linen tables already dotted with cocktails and conversation.

Sherry steps in—

—and stops.

Her breath catches, just slightly.
She’s been in the stadium before—**plenty of times.**
But she’s never been in *this part.*
This isn’t for fans. This is for **patrons**.
**Insiders.**

The far wall is lined with **framed photos**—grainy black and whites of the Big Red Machine in unguarded moments.
Sparky laughing with Joe Morgan.
Tony Pérez smoking a cigar in the locker room.
Bench and Rose mid-prank, shirts half off, beers in hand.

These weren’t shot from the stands.
These were taken *inside the story.*

The artwork is gallery-worthy—
painted portraits of Reds legends, mixed media installations, even a shadowbox featuring cleats from the '76 World Series.

> “Jeff,” she murmurs, “is that *actual* turf from Riverfront?”

Jeff glances at the display and shrugs, grinning.

> “Probably. Could be dirt from Crosley Field in somebody’s bourbon glass too.
They like to flex.”

And then—
she starts seeing the *people.*

Polished suits. Laughter too practiced. Rolexes and University Club lapel pins.
The **Cincinnati power crowd** in full display.

> “Oh my God,” she mutters. “That’s the mayor.
And isn’t that the Channel 9 weather guy? The one with the unfortunate eyebrows?”

Jeff leans in.

> “And over there’s the head of Fifth Third Bank.
And the Reds CFO.
And that guy runs three dealerships, two hospitals, and a bourbon label.”

Sherry blinks.

> “I’m underdressed.”

Jeff nudges her gently with his elbow.

> “You’re in the right hat. That’s all that matters.”

She takes it all in—one long, slow breath.
And suddenly, she’s not just attending Opening Day.
She’s **part of** it.
A player in the game.

And right beside her?
The man who handed her the golden ticket.

---
---

#### **SCENE: THE MAN FROM SATURDAY**

Sherry laughs politely at something Jeff says, still taking in the suite’s warm bustle, when her eyes catch a movement across the room.

**Him.**
The man from last Saturday.
Three dealerships.
The cologne that could start fires.
The handshake too firm.
The voice that said things without saying anything.

The man who slid her that cryptic little business card at the MAD fundraiser—
with words like *liar* and *despoiler* whispered between donated dollars and lukewarm Chipotle.

And now he’s here.
In a tailored jacket.
Talking to a local judge.
Acting like he hasn’t branded her brain with quiet suspicion.

Sherry stops breathing for a second.
**Still.**
Just a second.
Just long enough for Jeff to take another step forward without realizing she’s no longer at his side.

She glances to her left.

**The charcuterie board.**
Safe haven.
Olives and soft cheeses and plausible deniability.

> *“I need a cracker,”* she mutters to no one, already moving.

She doesn’t want confrontation.
Not here.
Not now.

Not while her pink hat still smells like fresh thread and a man beside her is offering something close to peace.

As she reaches for a tiny fork and pretends to ponder salami, she whispers to herself:

> *“You do not get to ruin this.
Not today.”*

---
---

#### **SCENE: MEAT & MYSTERY**

Sherry stands quietly at the charcuterie board, watching thin slices of prosciutto droop under the weight of the room.
Everything’s too elegant.
Too slow.
Too exposed.

Then—
**a plate.**
Set beside her.
Two small bison sliders stacked with care.

And next to them, the unmistakable blue label of **Kroger water.**
Frosted. Full.
Home.

She glances up.
Jeff.
Already taking a bite of his own slider, chewing like this is all perfectly normal.

> “You looked like someone who needed something simple,” he says, half-muffled.

Sherry smiles faintly, takes the water bottle, grateful for something familiar to hold.

> “Thanks. I did.”

He nods, doesn’t dig.
Just leans a hip on the table and scans the room like he’s trying to decide between a third slider or whatever that mystery dip near the olives might be.

After a moment, his voice lowers.

> “You okay?”

Sherry hesitates.
Then shrugs.

> “Just… saw someone I wasn’t expecting.”

Jeff doesn’t ask who.
He doesn’t have the context—he was across the world, in a time zone where this room didn’t exist.

> “Ah.
Didn’t mean to crash into something personal.”

> “You didn’t. You just—showed up right when I needed a break.”

He raises his bottle slightly in a faux-toast.

> “To accidental good timing.”

She taps hers against it.

> “And meat.”

He grins.

> “Always meat.”

She watches him for a second longer.
Steady. Present. Not prying.

> “You really didn’t have to do this.”

> “Sure I did.
This suite’s got two things I love—good food and you looking like you’re about to bolt.
Can’t let either one go to waste.”

---
---

#### **SCENE: THE WINDOW WALL & THE RIVER'S RHYTHM**

Jeff wipes his fingers on a napkin, nods toward the other end of the suite.

> “Come on. Walk with me.”

Sherry raises an eyebrow, already mid-sip of her water.

> “To where?”

> “Window. Big one. Giant one. The cathedral of glass they built for people like us to stare out of dramatically.”

He’s already moving.
She follows.

They weave past clusters of suits and laughter, the hum of opening day buzz dulled by thick carpet and the chill of air conditioning turned too high.

And then—
**the glass.**

A towering wall of it, stretching up fifty feet, running longer than the suite itself.
Beyond it, **the Ohio River.**

Wide. Brown. Glinting in the sun.
**Alive.**

Jeff stops at the edge, hands in his pockets.
Sherry stands beside him.

> “There,” he says. “Ignore the stadium for a second. Just look.”

She squints, unimpressed.

> “Jeff, I live in Kentucky.
I’ve got a pretty good idea what that river looks like.”

He grins, tilts his head just a bit.

> “Sure. But humor me.
Ignore Covington.
Ignore the skyline.
Ignore the traffic.”

He points.

> “See the barge?”

A low, lumbering vessel rumbles along the water, slow as a sermon.
Beyond it—small boats, sunlit and bobbing, with music barely audible even through glass.
People on deck, dancing. Laughing.
**Living.**

> “Look at *them*,” Jeff says softly.
> “They’re not thinking about taxes. Or RSVPs. Or email threads.
They’re having a damn good time.”

Sherry watches, the tension slowly unwinding from her shoulders.

> “Must be nice.”

Jeff glances at her.

> “Let’s steal some of it.
Let’s just… borrow a little of their joy.”

She turns, smiling despite herself.

> “Is that what we’re doing now? Joy theft?”

> “Yep.
I’m a felon. Lock me up.
But only if they serve sliders in prison.”

They stand in companionable silence, letting the river move below them, letting the suite fade behind them.

Just **two people**.

**No stage. No spotlight. Just space.**

---
---

#### **SCENE: WINDOW WHISPER, COLOR CONFESSION**

They’re standing at the edge of the world—
Fifty feet of glass in front of them, barges drifting below, the hum of a stadium behind them.

Jeff leans just a little closer.
Low voice. No warning.

> “You wearing a bra today?”

Sherry turns to him, a sharp look in her eyes—
equal parts challenge and curiosity.

> “Excuse me?”

Jeff’s grin spreads slow, easy.

> “Yeah.
You are.
I can see the outline when the light hits right.”

He tilts his head, studying her like she’s a riddle wrapped in pink cotton and sass.

> “What color?”

She narrows her eyes.

> “And what if I told you it’s beige and boring?”

He smirks.

> “Then I’d say you’re lying.
Because nothing about you is boring.
Especially not under that hat.”

She fights a smile.
Fails.
Rolls her eyes instead.

> “Pink. You win.”

> “Like your hat?”

> “Exactly like my hat.”

He lets that sit for a second.

> “That’s synergy.”

Sherry nudges him gently with her shoulder.

> “If you make one more marketing joke, I’m pushing you through this window.”

> “That’s fair.”

They fall quiet again, watching the water.
But now the air between them carries a little charge.
A little **color.**

---
---

#### **SCENE: THE WARNING, BY THE GLASS**

Jeff leans back against the glass, just a touch of mischief in his voice—
but something else behind his eyes.

> “The reason I asked about the bra…”

Sherry looks up at him, waiting.

> “…is because you’re about to be in sexual competition.”

She blinks.

> “Excuse me?”

Jeff raises an eyebrow.

> “If we’re the first ones here, and we’re pretending to be the hosts, then you’ve gotta be ready. Okay, Sherry?”

He lets that land.

She stares at him, skeptical.

> “Ready for what?”

> “For the looks. The assumptions.
The way people will glance at you, and then glance at me.
Some of them will want to figure out the power dynamic.
Some will want to figure out how to get between us.
A few may try.”

He’s calm.
Cool.
But not cold.

> “I’m not saying it to stress you out.
I’m saying it because you’re going to win.”

Sherry raises a brow.

> “Win what?”

Jeff grins.

> “The room.”

Beat.

> “So… pink bra, pink hat. You’ve already got the brand.
Just hold the line.”

She lets out a slow breath.

> “You are such a jackass.”

> “And you love it.”

> “Mmm.”

Jeff tilts his head.

> “Ready to play Queen of the Box?”

She glances back out at the barges.
And smiles.

> “Let’s burn it down.”

---
---

#### **SCENE: WHO’S COMING**

Sherry finishes the last of her water, the condensation warming in her hand.
Jeff leans his elbow against the glass, tone shifting slightly.
Less playful.
More grounded.

> “Alright, heads up. Couple folks you’re going to meet today.”

Sherry lifts an eyebrow.

> “Is this the part where I get nervous?”

> “Nah. Just the part where you get **informed**.”

He ticks them off casually, one finger at a time.

> “Kathy Espich’ll be here. Lead singer. You know. Goddess. Everyone falls in love with her at least once.”

Sherry smirks.

> “Including you?”

> “…That’s classified.”

She rolls her eyes. He continues.

> “Jim Brown—drummer. Human noise machine.
Loud. Funny. Might ask you ten personal questions in the first two minutes. Don’t let it faze you.”

> “Got it. Noise machine.”

> “My brother Jeremy—he’s around somewhere. Looks like me if I was an inch inches taller and still gave a damn about cardio.”

> “You already warned me about him.”

> “Yeah, he’s… intense. But good people.”

Then, a pause.
Jeff’s tone cools, just a bit.

> “Cremeans is coming too. Our manager.”

Sherry nods.

> “I’ve heard the name.”

> “You’ll know the type. Kentucky polite, zero bullshit.
Wears a collared shirt to mow his lawn.”

She laughs softly.

> “Sounds exhausting.”

> “It is. But he keeps us out of jail and off TMZ, so we keep him.”

He hesitates—then adds:

> “Don’t know if Jen’ll be here. His wife.
She’s—look, just be aware.
They don’t drink. They don’t swear.
They’re good people. But real square.”

Sherry tilts her head.

> “So… I shouldn’t offer them weed gummies and a threesome?”

Jeff nearly chokes on his own laugh.

> “You *can*, but I’m not bailing you out when she files a church petition to have you exorcised.”

> “Noted.”

He gives her a once-over. Not checking her out—just checking in.

> “You’re gonna be fine.
You’re smarter than all of ‘em. And way better dressed.”

She adjusts her pink Reds cap and gives him a slow smirk.

> “You sure?”

> “I’m sure.”

> “Even if I say *fuck* in front of Mrs. Cremeans?”

Jeff leans closer, lowers his voice to a whisper.

> “Just don’t do it while holding a cocktail and talking about birth control, and you’ll survive.”

---

#### **SCENE: KUBRICK, CLOAKS, AND SHOCK**

Jeff crosses his arms and gives her a sidelong glance.

> “You know why you don’t say *fuck* in front of Mrs. Cremeans?”

Sherry huffs a breath through her nose.

> “Hit me. You can’t possibly surprise me.
I didn’t even know she *existed* until like—fifteen seconds ago.”

Jeff leans just a little closer, voice dropping like it’s a classified secret.

> “Her favorite movie is *Eyes Wide Shut.*”

Sherry recoils like someone just whispered *human sacrifice*.

> “You’re lying.”

> “I wish I was.
She saw it five times.
With her husband.”

> “*Cremeans* sat through masked sex parties… five times?”

Jeff nods slowly, as if he’s still processing it all these years later.

> “Yup.
Even dragged me and my ex-wife along once.
Double date.
Red wine and orgies.”

> “No.”

> “Yes.”

> “NO.”

> “We left halfway through.
They stayed.
Got dessert afterward.”

Sherry puts a hand to her temple like she’s trying to erase the image.

> “Jesus. Do they have a secret room in their basement?”

Jeff shrugs.

> “I haven’t *not* wondered that.”

> “Please tell me they don’t own cloaks.”

> “Matching.
Maroon.
Velvet.
Embossed initials.”

> “I swear to God—”

> “Sherry, I’m telling you. You drop a ‘fuck’ in front of her, and her pupils dilate like she’s back in the theater.”

Sherry stares at him.

> “I am never saying *any* word with a hard ‘K’ sound around that woman.
I’ll stick to *please* and *thank you* and just point at snacks.”

Jeff chuckles low.

> “Wise choice.”

> “Did they *talk* about it afterward? Like, was there… analysis?”

> “Sherry, they called it *visionary cinema.*
They quoted it.
They had favorite *lines.*”

Sherry exhales.

> “Okay.
So… no *fuck* in front of Jen.
Got it.
Maybe just a soft ‘oh dear’ and a nod.”

Jeff smirks.

> “That’s the ticket.”

---

#### **SCENE: SIGNED, SEALED, SURREAL**

Sherry has her hand pressed against her temple, trying to banish the mental images Jeff just painted.

> “So let me get this straight—Mrs. Cremeans has seen *Eyes Wide Shut* five times…
with her husband?”

Jeff nods.

> “Yup.”

> “And you and your ex-wife went on a *double date* to that?”

> “Yup.”

> “I have so many questions and no healthy way to ask any of them.”

Jeff grins, clearly enjoying this.

> “Want to know the best part?”

Sherry lowers her hand and narrows her eyes.

> “This *gets* worse?”

> “After that double date, we’re in L.A., maybe a year later. I end up at this weird post-award show afterparty. Nicole Kidman’s there.”

> “*No.*”

> “Yes.”

> “NO.”

> “Sherry, I have a rolled-up *Eyes Wide Shut* poster in storage.
Autographed.
By.
Nicole.
Fucking.
Kidman.”

She stares at him like he’s grown antlers.

> “Why are you like this?”

> “She signed it: *To Jeff—Keep your eyes open.*”

Sherry puts her hand over her mouth, laughing so hard she doubles forward.

> “That’s not real. That can’t be real.”

> “I swear on all seven of Jim’s drum kits.”

> “Oh my God.
You’re just casually walking around with Kubrick memorabilia and I’m over here trying to remember how to spell *Cremeans.*”

Jeff leans in, voice low.

> “I haven’t even told you about the Tom Cruise story.”

> “Don’t. I will literally combust.”

> “Fair.”

Sherry exhales like she just survived a full-body spiritual exfoliation.

> “So no swearing in front of Jen, and if she mentions ‘cinema,’ I run.”

> “Correct.”

> “I’m gonna need more water.”

---

#### **SCENE: THE RULES**

They’re standing near the railing, the window stretching high above them, the sound of stadium prep rumbling just beneath the glass.

Jeff turns slightly, the edge of a grin fading into something far more focused.

> “Okay, Sherry. You’re about to learn the rules.”

Her brow knits, cautious.

> “What do you mean, *rules*?”

He holds up a hand, then taps the air with two fingers.

> “No. Not rules.
**THE**—”
He glances at her, emphasizing it with his eyes.
“—all caps—**RULES.**”

Sherry narrows her eyes.

> “You’re being weird.”

> “Fundamental.”

> “You’re being *dramatic.*”

> “That too.
Because if you don’t understand *THE* rules,
you will be *absolutely* lost.”

She shifts her weight, wary but intrigued.

> “Do I have your attention now?”

A beat.

> “Yeah.
You’ve got it.”

He exhales. Not tense—just serious.

> “Sherry, look around.
This world? This suite? These people?
There are layers.
Games.
Plays inside of plays.”

> “Is this a movie now?”

> “It always was.”

Sherry crosses her arms.

> “So what—are you the director?”

> “Hell no. I’m the unreliable narrator.”

> “Even better.”

Jeff’s voice drops just a little lower.

> “But seriously—
before anyone else gets here—
you need to understand the Rules.
Because otherwise,
you’ll spend the rest of the day asking the wrong questions.”

Sherry looks around—at the empty suite, the quiet anticipation.

> “Fine.
Tell me.
What are *The Rules*?”

Jeff smiles, slow and wicked.

> “Thought you’d never ask.”

---


#### **SCENE: THE RULES, PART I – THE NAMES**

Jeff leans against the back of a leather seat, arms crossed, tone somewhere between conspiratorial and exasperated.

> “Alright. Listen carefully.
Everybody in my social circle—everyone that matters—
has practically the same fucking name.”

Sherry tilts her head.

> “That sounds like a *you* problem.”

Jeff raises a finger.

> “Nope. It’s a *you’re-about-to-be-a-part-of-this-circle* problem.
So, let me help you survive it.”

He paces once, then gestures with both hands like he’s conducting an orchestra of idiocy.

> “You know me as Jeff Evans.
Cool. Normal. Manageable.
Except—our manager’s name is **Jeff Cremeans**.”

> “Two Jeffs?”

> “Correct.
Which is why he is *never* ‘Jeff.’
He is always **Cremeans.**
To his face. Behind his back.
Even in text threads.”

> “Okay…”

> “And his wife?
**Jen Cremeans.**
J-E-N.
Never Jeannette.
Don’t even think it.
We’ve banned that name from the goddamn narrative.
Jeannette never happened.
Jen is Jen. Always Jen.”

> “This feels like a cult.”

> “It *is*.
A cult of sanity prevention.”

Sherry raises an eyebrow, but he steamrolls ahead.

> “Now.
My brother? **Jeremy Evans.**
Tall, lean, uptight as hell.
He’s always Jeremy.
Never ‘Jerm.’ Never ‘Jer.’
God help you if you say ‘J-Dawg.’”

Sherry laughs.

> “Noted.”

> “Then we’ve got our best friend—Jeremy Gilley.
Bless the fuckin’ stars that he goes by **Gilley**, because otherwise,
we’d have *two Jeremys* in a single tour bus.
Which is how bands die, Sherry.
That’s how *wars start.*”

She’s openly grinning now. Jeff presses on, relentless.

> “And the drummer?
**Jim Brown.**
Not the godfather of soul.
Not the Hall of Fame running back.
Just a kid from Park Lane who plays drums like his soul is on fire
and has a totally inappropriate obsession with Phil Collins.”

> “That’s… specific.”

> “We’ve had to stage interventions.
He’s got Phil Collins vinyls *in plastic*.
But I digress.”

> “I’m barely hanging on.”

Jeff stops and points at her.

> “Good. That means you’re *ready.*
You now understand the most critical survival system in our social architecture:
**name etiquette.**”

> “Wait—what do they call *me*?”

He grins.

> “That depends.
Do you want to be *Sherry*…
or do you want to be *Sherry, the girl with no last name who walks in like she owns the fuckin' suite*?”

Sherry smirks.

> “I want to be the girl they remember tomorrow.”

> “Then remember the names.
And wear that hat like it’s a crown.”

---

#### **SCENE: THE RULES, PART II – THE NAMES NEVER STOP**

Jeff lets his fingers trace the condensation on his water bottle. Then looks back at her, voice dry.

> “You think the name thing’s bad now?”

Sherry lifts a brow.

> “I’m already struggling to hold the org chart in my brain.”

He snorts.

> “In high school?
It was worse.
I had friends named Jeff Nottingham, Jeff Pryor, and Jeff Koleczkowski.
We could have played a whole goddamn Euchre game with just four Jeffs.”

Sherry chuckles.

> “That sounds like a cult.”

> “It was. A sweaty, hormonal, card-slinging cult.
And then we’d have Jeff on the left, waiting to deal himself in if someone had to take a leak.
Which Jeff? Didn’t matter.
Always another Jeff in the wings.”

He pauses.

> “And down the street? Jeremy Dawson.”

> “Another Jeremy?”

> “Yep.
And Jeremy Dawson was married to a woman we do *not* speak about.”

> “Why?”

Jeff shakes his head.

> “Sherry.
We carry grudges.”

She goes still.

> “We?”

> “Commuted.
The guys.
And the woman.
Over the woman.
We carry grudges like they’re sacred relics.
We do *not* forget.
We do *not* forgive.
And if it came to it—”
He leans forward, voice dropping to a velvet hush,
“—we’d stick a Bowie knife right between your ribs.”

Sherry stares at him.

> “You’re joking.”

> “Try me.”

He straightens up and smiles, warm again, like nothing happened.

> “Anyway. Want another slider?”

---

#### Scene: *The Suite, 90 Minutes to Game Time*

Jeff’s in rare form—setting plates, arranging swag, casually tuning the room like a seasoned bartender tunes a crowd.

The river outside sparkles. The city buzzes below.

The suite is perfect.
**Too perfect.**

He’s got that look on his face.
That subtle Jeff look that says:
*“Something’s about to break loose, and I’m going to enjoy it either way.”*

**Then—Jeremy enters.**
Carrying two **impossibly cold bottles** of actual German beer.

> **Jeff:** “You brought foreign beer to Opening Day?”
> **Jeremy:** “This *is* Opening Day. Think of it as diplomatic relations.”
> **Jeff:** “You’re an ambassador of barley.”
> **Jeremy:** “And you’re the Secretary of Snacks. Where’s my charcuterie?”

They toast.

The suite has sliders.
It has pulled pork.
It has *sushi*.
It has *Kathy incoming*, *Sherry watching*, *the Reds warming up*,
and **not a single goddamn napkin in sight.**

> **Jeremy (raising a brow):**
> “Who’s here already?”
> **Jeff:** “No one that’ll make us fight. Yet.”
> **Jeremy:** “So. Sherry?”
> **Jeff:** “Yep.”
> **Jeremy:** “Kathy?”
> **Jeff (drinks deeply):** “…Incoming.”
> **Jeremy:** “You magnificent idiot.”

They clink bottles again.

This is the last moment of peace before all the lions enter the coliseum.

And both Evans brothers know it.

---

#### Scene: *Two Predators Meet Over German Beer and Unspoken History*

Jeremy’s leaned against the glass, bottle in hand, scanning the ballpark…
…when he hears the door behind him.
He turns.

> **Jeremy:** “Who the fuck are you?”

No smile. No warmth. Just **a family test** being issued.

Sherry blinks.
Straightens her back.
Sizes him right the hell back.

> **Sherry:** “The woman boning your brother. Who the fuck are you?”

Jeremy grins.
*There it is.*
**She passed.**
He sees it now—why Jeff looks a little *lighter* these days.
Why the text tone changed.

He tilts his head, nods once.

> **Jeremy:** “You sound like us.”
> **Sherry:** “You sound like Jeff.”
> **Jeremy:** “I am Jeff, but better looking, better dressed, and with fewer lawsuits.”
> **Sherry:** “Definitely an asshole, then.”
> **Jeremy (grinning):** “You’re not wrong.”

Jeff watches from across the suite.
Two apex predators sniffing each other out.
And instead of blood—
**they find kinship.**

> **Sherry (to Jeff):**
> “Okay, I get it now.
> I was wondering if you came out of a mold or a lab.
> But nope.
> It’s a bloodline thing.”

> **Jeremy:** “She’s your kind of people, Jeff.”
> **Jeff (already smiling):** “Told you.”

They don’t hug.
They don’t shake hands.
They just stand there, three-pointed star of chaos and charm,
**waiting for the game… and the goddamn drama… to begin.**

---

#### Scene: *Suite. Early Game Banter. The Brothers Evans Expose Their IQs.*

Jeremy swigs his beer, leans against the table like he owns the whole fucking suite.

> **Jeremy:**
> “You know I’m the smarter one, right?”

Sherry raises a brow. Jeff doesn’t even blink.

> **Jeremy (to Sherry):**
> “He may have the voice, the face, the stage legs—but up here?”
> *[taps his temple]*
> “I’m the brains.”

> **Jeff (without looking up):**
> “This is the guy who tanked on *Celebrity Jeopardy.*”

> **Sherry (perking up):**
> “Wait, for real?”

> **Jeremy (defensive):**
> “It was buzzer lag.”

> **Jeff (mocking):**
> “*I’ll make it a true Daily Double, Alex.*”
> *Pause.*
> “The category was ‘Your Own Damn Name.’”

> **Jeremy (grinning):**
> “Screw you. I was drunk. I had altitude sickness.”

> **Jeff:**
> “It filmed in Burbank.”

> **Sherry (cracking up):**
> “Oh my God. You two are terrible.”

> **Jeremy (raising his bottle):**
> “And genetically unavoidable.”

---

Jeff smirks.
Jeremy does a half-bow.
Sherry watches both of them and thinks:

> *“These idiots might actually be magic.”*

And she’s not wrong.
**Commuted’s backbone is right here.**

---

#### Scene: *The Suite — Now With Historical Warfare*

Jeff tosses a bottle cap into a trash can without looking.

> **Jeff:**
> “You know who *didn’t* choke on a Daily Double?”
> “The First Minnesota.”

> **Jeremy (instantly engaged):**
> “Oh, *here we go.*”

Sherry: *“…what?”*

> **Jeff (warming up):**
> “July 2nd, 1863. Gettysburg. Union center’s about to collapse. Lee’s boys pushing straight through the Peach Orchard. Everything’s falling apart—except one unit.”

> **Jeremy (with a flourish):**
> “One regiment. **262 men.** That’s it.”

> **Jeff:**
> “General Hancock looks around and says: *‘I need five minutes.’* And who steps up?”

> **Jeremy (grinning):**
> “The **goddamn 1st Minnesota.**”

Sherry holds up her hands.

> **Sherry:**
> “Wait—how do you both know this?”

> **Jeff:**
> “Because it’s the hardest flex in military history.”

> **Jeremy:**
> “They charged an entire Confederate brigade to *stall them.* Outnumbered *ten to one.* They knew they were gonna die—**and they charged anyway.**”

> **Jeff (suddenly serious):**
> “They bought Hancock five minutes. The Union line held.”

> **Jeremy (raising his bottle like a toast):**
> “**82% casualty rate.** The highest of the entire war. But they held.”

Silence.

Then Sherry:
> “Okay, that was hot. And weird. But mostly hot.”

> **Jeff (grinning):**
> “We’re full of surprises.”

> **Jeremy:**
> “Also, I can name every commander at Antietam in order of when they lost their shit.”

> **Sherry:**
> “Now *that’s* the sexiest thing you’ve ever said.”

**Two Civil War nerds. One slightly alarmed, slightly turned-on woman.**
Peak Evans energy.

---

#### Scene: *Antietam Flex & the Gentle Mercy of Restraint*

Jeremy, still sipping that pristine German beer, grins like a man who’s been waiting his whole life to show off this useless brilliance.

> **Jeremy (with mock reverence):**
> “Alright.
> Joseph Mansfield. Twelfth Corps. Shot in the gut.
> Ambrose Burnside. Ninth Corps. Couldn’t cross a fucking bridge.
> Edwin Sumner. Second Corps. Charged too early. Got slaughtered.
> Joseph Hooker. First Corps. Got knocked out by an artillery shell before lunch.”

He pauses.

Raises a brow at Sherry.
**Waits.**

> **Sherry:**
> “…Go on?”

> **Jeremy (grinning):**
> “Nah.
> When someone says, *‘that’s the sexiest thing you’ve ever said,’* it’s not an invitation to recite the whole goddamn order of battle.”

> **Jeff (smirking):**
> “Growth. Look at you. Not being an entire nerd.”

> **Jeremy (deadpan):**
> “I’m evolving. Next I’ll have emotions.”

Sherry exhales hard through her nose, caught somewhere between admiration and *“what the hell is happening right now.”*

They’re **weird.**
They’re **hot.**
They’re **dangerous in packs.**

---

#### Scene: *Suite. 30 Minutes to First Pitch. And Then — Kathy.*

The door hisses open.

No knock.
No warning.
Just **a presence.**

**Kathy Espich.**

---

She’s draped in **something red**—
not Reds red, not corporate-approved merchandise—
but a **red that screams sin** in slow motion.
A silk wrap, or a dress, or maybe it’s just expensive smoke clinging to skin.

Her legs go on forever.
Her heels are criminal.
And **if she’s wearing underwear**, it's **either invisible or fictional.**

Sherry blinks once, hard.
Then again.

> **Sherry (to herself):**
> *“Oh my god. Is she even wearing—”*

Jeremy mutters under his breath.

> **Jeremy:**
> “Jesus Christ.”

Jeff doesn’t move.

Not a flinch. Not a twitch. Not a goddamn syllable.

He knew this was coming.
He’s just trying not to **get pulled into orbit.**

> **Kathy (purring):**
> “Gentlemen. Sherry.”

She smiles with lips that know secrets.
**All the secrets.**
And she walks past Jeff without touching him—
**but the electricity lingers anyway.**

---

Sherry straightens her spine.
Her competitive instincts fire like a switchblade.
Because this isn’t just inappropriate for a ballpark.
This is a **declaration of war** in silk and sinew.

> **Sherry (to herself):**
> *“You have *got* to be kidding me.”*

---

The suite, once relaxed, once familial—
is now **a jungle of sex and memory and silent challenge.**

Jeff still hasn’t said a word.

Sherry wonders—
**who taught him to stay this still?**

Answer: **Kathy.**


---

#### Scene: *The Air Just Got Cut With a Razor Blade*

Kathy’s smile has weight.
She turns slightly, her lips still curled in a way that might be polite. Might be predatory.

And Sherry, boots planted, voice low and steady—

> **Sherry:**
> “How the hell do you know my name, Miss S-Bitch?”

Silence.

Even Jeremy looks up from his beer.

Jeff winces, but only slightly.
This is what happens when you bring **gasoline and matches** into the same room.

Kathy doesn’t blink.

> **Kathy (sweet as arsenic):**
> “Oh, honey. I know *everyone’s* name. Especially the ones my exes are sleeping with.”

That lands.
Quiet like a sniper bullet.

> **Sherry (flat):**
> “You must be tired of keeping up. Or is this just a Google Alert thing for you now?”

Jeremy coughs.
Jeff finally opens his mouth.

> **Jeff:**
> “Okay, let’s not open the inning with a bench-clearing brawl.”

> **Kathy (not taking her eyes off Sherry):**
> “Just saying hi.”

> **Sherry:**
> “Next time? Just wave.”

---

#### Scene: *Suite — The Quiet Word That Isn’t*

Jeff catches Kathy by the elbow, leans in close, voice low and sharp.

> **Jeff:**
> “Not the time, not the place.”

> **Kathy (mischievous, wicked):**
> “You say that like there *is* a right time.”

> **Jeff:**
> “Jesus, Kathy.”

She glances over his shoulder, right at Sherry, who hasn’t moved—
but whose entire body is clearly a wire pulled taut.

> **Kathy (playful):**
> “She’s kinda cute, Jeff. Sweet boots. I bet she’s got… stamina.”

> **Jeff (dead serious):**
> “Don’t.”

> **Kathy:**
> “What? I’m being generous. Thought I’d offer a *welcome-to-the-suite* gift.”

> **Jeff:**
> “A threesome?”

> **Kathy (grinning like sin itself):**
> “Well. You’ve already had me. Might as well let her see what all the fuss was about.”

---

Jeff just closes his eyes.

He’s not mad.
He’s not amused.
He’s just **bone-deep exhausted** by the Kathy Espich Experience.

> **Jeff:**
> “You make everything into a game.”

> **Kathy (leaning closer):**
> “Correction: I make everything *interesting.* You’re the one who came back for more.”

He sighs.

Meanwhile—
**Sherry is still watching.**
Trying to read lips.
Trying to hold her ground.
Trying to figure out if she’s being **recruited or tested or hunted.**

---

#### Scene: *Sherry, Realizing the Pull of the Black Hole in Heels*

Sherry’s arms are crossed.
Boots planted.
Jaw clenched so hard she might crack a molar.

She watches them talk.

She doesn’t hear it.
But she doesn’t need to.

**Kathy leans in. Jeff looks down. Kathy smirks. Jeff sighs.**

And Sherry?
**Sherry gets it.**

> **Sherry (to herself):**
> *“Oh my God. He wasn’t kidding.”*

She thought it was a metaphor.
She thought *“black hole”* meant drama or history or unfinished business.

But no.

**This is gravity.**
This is mass.
This is the slow, impossible pull of someone who *always gets the center of the room.*

> **Sherry (still internal):**
> *“You don’t resist her. You just learn how not to drown.”*

And worse—
Sherry can feel it **tugging at her, too.**
Kathy isn’t just magnetic to men.
She’s magnetic to **everyone.**

---

> **Sherry (again, internal):**
> *“If I had met her at a bar on a normal night… I might have said yes.”*

And now?
Now she’s watching Kathy *maybe* flirt with her boyfriend
while also *maybe* flirt with *her.*

And Sherry realizes:
**this is going to be war.**
But it might also be…
**fun.**

---

#### Scene: *Sherry Stews. And Then Jim Brown Happens.*

Sherry’s still trying to wrap her head around Kathy-fucking-Espich.
Trying to make sense of the shimmer in Jeff’s eyes.
Trying to understand the *pull* and why her own boots suddenly feel unsteady.

And then—
the suite door swings **wide open.**

> **Jim Brown:**
> “Hey assholes! You’d never believe the traffic on Fort Washington—”

He doesn’t get another word out.
Because both Jeff and Jeremy **descend like velociraptors**.

> **Jeremy:**
> “NOPE. No greeting. No peace. Not when you’re wearing that.”

> **Jeff:**
> “Is that a Cardinals hat?! In *this* house?!”

Jim yells something incoherent—
possibly a plea, possibly a threat, possibly a declaration of war—
but the brothers have him halfway into a headlock and a very undignified tickle assault
before he can set his beer down.

Sherry **blinks hard**.

Kathy laughs.
A low, smoky laugh that sounds like it came from another lifetime.

And just like that—
**the tension in the room doesn’t go away…
but it splinters.**

Fractures into **energy.**
Into **motion.**
Into **everything that comes with being in Commuted’s orbit.**

> **Sherry (internally):**
> *“This is what I signed up for.
> These lunatics. These legends.
> This was a mistake.
> This is the best mistake I’ve ever made.”*

---

#### Scene: *He Walked in Like Smoke*

The suite is still laughing.
Jeff and Jeremy are shoving Jim around, arguing about who’s responsible for the slider sauce on the carpet.
Kathy is leaning against the bar like a goddess bored of Olympus.

And then—
**he walks in.**

Not rushed.
Not loud.

Just… **smoke.**

> **Sherry (to herself):**
> *“Come on, come on, come on…”*
> It’s not a lyric.
> It’s his **walk.**

A half-smirk like he knows the end of the story.
Boots that don’t squeak—**they claim territory.**
A black t-shirt with no logo, no slogan—**just skin and silhouette.**
And eyes that…
**see. Everything.**

> **Sherry (internal, breathless):**
> *“I thought Jeff was hot…”*

And now she understands.

She understands why Jeff **defers** to someone else.
Why even Kathy straightens up—just slightly—when *he* walks in.

> **Sherry:**
> “Is that—?”

Jeff nods, not even turning around.

> **Jeff:**
> “Gilley.”

---

**Gilley doesn’t make noise.**
The room just *gets quieter* to make space for him.

> **Gilley (low):**
> “Hope someone saved me a beer. Or a soul.”

> **Jeremy (calling out):**
> “You’re five minutes late, Mephisto. We already gave up our souls.”

Gilley walks toward the bar, unbothered.
He tips his chin at Sherry—*not a greeting, a recognition.*
Like he already knows who she is, and what she’s about,
and **what she might taste like.**

> **Sherry (to herself):**
> *“Oh.
> This one?
> This one’s going to wreck me.”*

---

#### Scene: *Sherry’s Brainwaves Just Got Rewritten*

The suite doesn’t spin.
That’s not how this works.
It **tilts.**

Everything moves a half-inch to the left—
into **his** orbit.

> **Sherry (internal, breath firing fast):**
> *Nope. Nope. Nope. Nope. Nope.*
> *Not gonna. Not gonna. Not gonna. Not gonna.*
> *…oh dear fuck I’m wet.*

Because she’s not dumb.
She’s been around.
She’s had rockstars, salesmen, **even the dentist once** flirt with her.

But *this?*

This is something **biblical.**

He hasn’t even said more than one sentence.
He hasn’t even **looked** at her like a wolf yet.
But she knows—
**oh God, she knows—**
if he said “follow me,” she’d ask how far.

> **Sherry (grabbing a glass of water to steady her hand):**
> *“Jesus. If this is Mephisto, he brought the fucking flames.”*

She glances at Jeff.

He’s talking to Kathy again, not watching her.
Not watching **Gilley.**

Which is good.

Because **Sherry needs thirty seconds to recalibrate her universe.**

---

#### Scene: *Jeff Intercepts the Spiral*

Jeff is laughing. Or pretending to.
Something Kathy said. Something flippant and sharpened.

But his eyes?
They’re scanning.

And then they land on Sherry.

The way her glass is still.
The way her eyes have locked.
The *tilt* of her knees.
The **very subtle spread of her thighs.**

> **Jeff (internally):**
> *Goddamn it. I’ve seen this before.*

*1990.
Kimberly Kessler.
Homecoming.
Backseat of Gilley’s mom’s Ford.*
*History fucking repeats itself.*

Jeff excuses himself mid-sentence.
Kathy keeps talking.
Because Kathy always keeps talking.

But Jeff beelines straight for **his date.**

---

> **Jeff (smiling too wide, hand on her waist):**
> “So. Enjoying the band’s little family reunion?”

Sherry jolts. A little too fast. A little too guilty.

> **Sherry (covering, poorly):**
> “I—uh—yep. Yeah. No. I mean, yes. Just… a lot.”

> **Jeff (quiet, low, measured):**
> “That’s Gilley. That’s what he does.
> He walks in and *everyone* gets a little… off-kilter.”

> **Sherry (not quite looking away):**
> “You said he was dangerous.”

> **Jeff:**
> “I also said I know how to keep you safe.”

---

Jeff leans in.
His voice, only for her now.

> **Jeff:**
> “You’re mine tonight, Sherry Sims Greene.
> And I’m not sharing. Not even with Mephisto.”

---

#### Scene: *The W.O. Wright’s Cocksuck Heard Round the Band*

Jeremy senses it.
Doesn’t need a signal. Doesn’t need a nod.
**He just knows.**

Jeff’s losing her.
And **Gilley’s not even trying.**

So Jeremy steps up like a goddamn bard with a blood vendetta.

> **Jeremy (loud, cheerful, slapping a hand on the nearest countertop):**
> “So hey, Sherry!
> You wanna hear the greatest story in the history of live music and mild public indecency?”

Sherry blinks.

> **Sherry (warily):**
> “Do I?”

> **Jeremy:**
> “Too late. You’re in it now.”

He grabs a slider off a plate, chews, and launches:

> **Jeremy:**
> “Picture it—July 1990.
> W.O. Wright’s, just outside Fairborn, Ohio.
> Our very first gig. We were loud, shitty, and *ready.*”

> “The place was packed with maybe two hundred twenty people who weren’t sure if we were a real band or just guys who stole instruments from the mall.”

> “Gilley—**Jeremy Fucking Gilley**—had just played a three-minute solo that was so good we thought the amps were going to set on fire.”

> “Set break hits.
> And this girl—**Stacey Dawson**—drags him behind the building like she’s possessed by horny demons.”

> “Ten minutes later, he comes back on stage, bass in hand, *grinning like he’d invented sex.*
> And the next song we played?
> **It was our best song of the night.**
> Something about a blowjob just… tunes your rhythm.”

---

Jeff exhales through his nose, grateful.
Gilley just smirks.

> **Gilley (cool as hell):**
> “I didn’t even get her number.”

> **Sherry (half-laughing, half-mortified, 100% overstimulated):**
> “You people are *deranged.*”

> **Jeremy:**
> “No.
> We’re *legends.*”

---

#### Scene: *The Panty Line Heard 'Round the Suite*

There’s a breath of silence.

That *slow drawl,* like the fuse is lit and the dynamite’s under someone else’s bed.

#### Scene: *The Correction Heard Round the Suite*

Jim’s riding the wave of being the “grown-up drummer,”

Quiet. Precise. Lethal.

**Jeremy (low to Sherry):**

**Sherry, watching this, thinks:**

Sherry stands near the glass, plastic cup of water in hand,

Kathy’s just **asserted academic dominance** like she was dropping a live grenade with pearls on.
Jeremy is **being Jeremy**—a dazzling blur of chaos and charisma wrapped in smug laughter.

Charming. Dry-witted. Calm in a room full of metaphorical flamethrowers.

**Watching.**
Reading the room.

The room hums with post-roast electricity.

Even Jeff’s visibly impressed.

Adjusts her sleeve like she’s about to deliver a TED Talk.

Sherry doesn’t blink.

That pulse of heat down her spine.
That frozen razor of fear *and* thrill.

> **Jeremy (low, near a whisper):**
> “She’s testing you.

#### Scene: *No Flinch*

The room’s in lockdown.
Eyes bouncing like pinballs between Sherry and Kathy.

> “You just showed me where to aim.”

On the wrists.

Jen’s eyes crinkle with amusement.

> **Jen:**
> “I *did* have a drink. Once. When Jeff got married. Only once. And it was just for the toast. It… meant something. But I’ll be honest—”

She makes a face, half grimace, half exaggerated betrayal.

> **Jen:**
> “—it sucked. Burned like regret. Tasted like floor cleaner. Never again.”

> **Sherry (grinning):**
> “That’s the most wholesome alcohol story I’ve ever heard.”

> **Jen (wry):**
> “It still got me a headache and a stomachache. Same as guilt. Same as bad company. Same as watching your best friend throw herself into a fire.”

They let that sit between them for a second—neither one entirely sure if Jen is still talking about gin.

Then, gently:

> **Jen:**
> “So no. I don’t drink gin. I drink coffee. Strong. Black. No sugar, no cream. Like the truth. And I keep my feet planted firmly on the ground… while everyone else here plays in the clouds.”

Jen glances toward the food table—checking to make sure no one’s getting too close to the good sushi—and then leans in slightly, like she’s ready to confide something playful, a secret for just the two of them.

> **Jen (grinning):**
> “Okay, you want to know how normal I really am?”

> **Sherry (teasing):**
> “You’re secretly addicted to *The Bachelor*?”

> **Jen:**
> “God, no. I have standards. But I *am* totally, unapologetically obsessed with Nicole Kidman.”

Sherry blinks—of all the things she expected, that wasn’t it.

> **Sherry:**
> “Like… Moulin Rouge Nicole? Or *Eyes Wide Shut* Nicole?”

Jen’s eyes sparkle mischievously.

> **Jen:**
> “Yes.”

> **Sherry (laughs):**
> “That’s not an answer.”

> **Jen (playful and sharp):**
> “Nicole Kidman is the bar. The high bar. The alpha and omega of female performance. She’s a chameleon, she’s classy, she’s fearless. That woman did *The Others* and *The Stepford Wives* and then turned around and did *Paddington*. That’s range.”

> **Sherry:**
> “So you’re saying she’s your role model?”

> **Jen (mock serious):**
> “No, I’m saying if I could trade places with any woman for one week, I’d choose Nicole Kidman *before* the voice of reason kicked in.”

> **Sherry (grinning):**
> “And what would you do with that week?”

Jen just gives her a sly little smile.

> **Jen:**
> “Wouldn’t you like to know.”

> **Sherry (deadpan):**
> “Not if it involves Tom Cruise.”

> **Jen (with an exaggerated shudder):**
> “Oh Lord, no. I’m talking about the post-Cruise era. *Big Little Lies* Kidman. The *undo him with one look and turn your spine to jelly* version.”

> **Sherry:**
> “…That’s oddly specific.”

Jen lifts her Kroger-brand water bottle and clinks it gently against Sherry’s.

> **Jen:**
> “Normal, remember? Red-blooded, well-adjusted, American. We’ve all got our girl crushes. Mine just happens to have an Oscar and better skin than should be legal.”

---

Sherry leaned a little closer to Jen, who was casually sorting sushi options at the edge of the buffet.

**Sherry**: “I’ve seen *Eyes Wide Shut*. And *Billy Bathgate*. Nicole Kidman’s naked quite a lot in both of those.”

Jen turned slightly, her expression unreadable for a second. Then, with the kind of calm honesty that seemed to catch Sherry off guard all afternoon, she replied:

**Jen**: “So am I.”

Sherry blinked. Not shocked—this was a suite full of rock stars and chaos—but genuinely caught off guard.

**Sherry**: “Wait… what?”

Jen smiled softly, shrugging like she’d just commented on the weather.

**Jen**: “Well, I’m married. I’ve had three kids. If you think modesty survives that process, you’re dreaming.”

Sherry let out a laugh, the kind that escaped like pressure from a valve.

**Sherry**: “Okay, that was not what I expected.”

**Jen** (smirking): “I said I’m normal, not vanilla.”

Sherry studied her. The outfit was modest. The tone was unassuming. But there was something steely there—something grounded, some kind of deep self-assurance that came from living life on her own terms in a storm of very loud people.

**Jen** (gently): “Being naked doesn’t make you wild. Being unashamed does.”

For a second, Sherry didn’t know how to respond. The words hit with more resonance than she expected.

Then Jen glanced toward the charcuterie setup and rolled her eyes.

**Jen**: “Excuse me—I see someone’s about to mix ginger with the wrong wasabi and I simply cannot stand idly by.”

She stepped away, leaving Sherry standing in the wake of one more unexpected truth bomb in a suite full of walking contradictions.

---

Jeff nudges his brother with his elbow, the universal “watch this” signal. Jeremy’s already watching. The two of them, posted up in the corner like they owned the place—and in a weird way, they kind of did—grinned like kids pulling a prank at the grown-ups’ table.

Sherry, halfway between the buffet and the bar, froze for a second, catching both of them in her periphery. She narrowed her eyes. Jeff raised his plastic cup, toasting her, and Jeremy gave a slow, mocking clap, barely more than a golf clap. Their grins were unmistakable: *We did this to you.*

She glared.

Jeff mouthed: “Nicole Kidman?”

Jeremy nearly doubled over, whispering something to Jeff that made both men burst out laughing. Jeff had to steady himself on the wall, shoulders shaking.

Sherry flipped them both off.

They howled harder.

It wasn’t cruelty. Not quite. It was the kind of laugh that said *you’re in the deep end now, sweetheart*—a kind of rite of passage. And Sherry, standing there in her jeans and pink Reds cap, realized something both exasperating and deeply satisfying:

She was in.

And they were going to make damn sure she earned it.

---

Sherry narrowed her eyes immediately, halfway between defensive and intrigued. The trap was obvious. The tone, baiting. Jeremy leaned in, elbows on the bar, beer in hand, with a grin that could cut glass.

**Jeremy**: “If you had to pick the *horniest* woman in this room…”

He dragged the word out like a fishing line.

**Jeremy**: “…the most *flexible* woman…”

He glanced at Jeff, smirking.

**Jeremy**: “…the most…”

**Jeremy (mocking)**: “Help me out here, big brother.”

Jeff, already rubbing the bridge of his nose like this was about to go sideways but unable to stop smiling, offered dryly:

**Jeff**: “Sexually inventive.”

**Jeremy** (pointing): “That’s it. The most sexually inventive. If you had to pick her out of this suite… who would you pick?”

Sherry let the silence stretch just long enough. Her eyes moved—methodically—around the room. Kathy was holding court by the window like she’d never met a spotlight she didn’t like. Jen was deep in conversation about homeschooling. There were women near the sushi, a couple at the bar. A few Sherry didn’t even recognize.

Then she looked back at the two brothers, folded her arms, and tilted her head.

**Sherry**: “Well, it sure as hell isn’t Jen. I’ve seen cornstarch with more edge.”

Jeremy nearly spit his drink. Jeff barked a surprised laugh.

**Sherry** (still calm): “And it’s not me. At least not today.”

She flicked her gaze toward Kathy.

**Sherry**: “But I’ve been in the same room with her for less than an hour and I already feel like I’m a prop in one of her fantasies. So… if we’re betting?”

A beat.

**Sherry**: “Put your money on Miss Espich.”

Jeremy whistled, slow and low.

**Jeremy**: “Goddamn. She *is* sharp.”

**Jeff**: “Told you.”

Sherry, finally grinning:

**Sherry**: “You two assholes always do this to the new people?”

**Jeremy** (deadpan): “Only the ones we like.”

**Jeff** (grinning like a man who knows he's about to cause whiplash):
“Nope. Sorry, Sherry. That would be *Jen Cremeans*.”

Sherry blinked, completely thrown.

**Jeff**:
“She’s got just about every kink that’s ever been in the… uh, what’s that book, Jeremy?”

**Jeremy** (not missing a beat):
“*Funkin’ Wagnalls*, baby.”

**Jeff** (nodding):
“Yeah. That one. That’s why we put you up to it.”

**Sherry** (jaw slightly slack):
“You’re joking.”

**Jeff** (raising a finger):
“Rule number seven, Sherry: Never judge a book by its cover.”

**Jeremy** (with a reverent shake of his head):
“Seventeen years married. And I swear to God, they probably fuck *daily*. Like clockwork. It’s terrifying.”

**Jeff** (to Jeremy):
“You remember that story about the Sunday School picnic and the—”

**Jeremy** (hands up, cutting him off):
“Don’t. Just don’t. That one’s still seared into my frontal lobe.”

Sherry sat back slowly, absorbing it all.

**Sherry**:
“Okay. Mental note: Be *very* careful around the quiet ones.”

**Jeff** (smiling):
“That’s not a note. That’s a fucking life philosophy.”

---

**“Ladies and gentlemen, to honor America, please rise and remove your caps.”**

The words crackled over the loudspeakers like thunder on a clear day, rolling through the open air of Great American Ballpark and echoing into the luxury suites above.

Inside Suite 14, a sudden hush fell. Conversations faltered. Half-eaten bites were paused in mid-air.

Jeff, standing closest to the window, was the first to move. He set his drink down with care, took off his battered Cincinnati Reds cap—a soft relic worn with time—and rose to his feet, tall and straight.

Jeremy followed without missing a beat, right hand pressed over his chest like it was second nature.

Sherry, startled by the instant shift in energy, glanced around the room and stood quickly. She didn’t have a cap, but her posture straightened, respectful.

Even Kathy, who had seemed above it all just moments earlier, rose smoothly and silently. Her arms stayed loose at her sides, but her expression was appropriately still.

Behind them, others followed. Jim Brown. Gilley. The Cremeanses, mid-sushi bite, paused and rose in tandem, like some married couple born of synchronized etiquette.

The stadium announcer continued, voice cutting clean through the crowd:  **“To honor America with the performance of our national anthem, please welcome local artist Marisa Weller.”**

From the far corner of the outfield, the first clear notes of *The Star-Spangled Banner* began to rise.

A lone voice, trembling just slightly, began to sing.  On the field below, a massive American flag—so wide it took two dozen volunteers to hold—rippled in the morning breeze.

Inside the suite, 40,000 hearts seemed to beat in unison.

Jeff removed his sunglasses, stared straight out the glass. Jeremy didn’t move a muscle. Sherry found her own heartbeat slowing, steadying. She hadn’t expected this—a civic stillness, a binding pause.

No one spoke. Not Kathy. Not Gilley. Not even Jen Cremeans, who looked like she might be crying softly but silently.

Outside the window, boats floated on the Ohio River, still for once. And beyond it, Covington looked smaller than ever.

The anthem climbed.
**“…And the rocket’s red glare…”**

And for a moment—just a moment—Sherry felt it: this wasn’t just spectacle.

**This was sacred.**

Opening Day in Cincinnati.
Baseball as religion.
Silence as reverence.

She placed her hand over her heart.

Because here, this mattered.

---

**“…and the rockets’ red glare…”**

A sudden thump rolled through the stadium’s floor. Then, a split-second later—

**BOOM.**

The sky above Great American Ballpark erupted in white light.

**“…the bombs bursting in air…”**

More detonations followed, each louder and more relentless than the last—like thundercracks hurled from the heavens. Red, white, and blue fireworks sprayed over the Ohio River, igniting the gray morning sky with reckless brilliance. Reflections danced on the water below, echoing each explosion like ripples of patriotic madness.

Sherry jumped. So did half the luxury suite. The glass rattled in its massive frames.

Jeff didn’t flinch.

He tilted his cap toward her and murmured, “This is Opening Day, babe. They always bring the boom.”

Below, forty-five thousand people stood as one. Hands on hearts. Heads bowed. Eyes skyward.

The anthem’s final words roared over the speakers:

**“O’er the land of the free…”**

The last volley of fireworks tore the air wide open.

**“…and the home of the brave.”**

Then—silence. Deafening, proud, perfect silence.

And the game was about to begin.

---

The suite didn’t just *look* like a high-roller’s retreat—it *was* one. The band had shelled out nearly $80,000 for the box, just for this one game. A staggering number, unless you considered what the Reds were after: repeat business. There were 81 home games a season, and 81 suites to sell each night. That was nearly $70 million in potential revenue. So yeah, they rolled out the red carpet.

And the wine? Not your usual ballpark swill. This wasn’t the watered-down house red poured in plastic cups from a questionable spigot. No, this was top-shelf—crisp, full-bodied, served chilled in actual glassware. The kind of wine that let you know your money had been *noticed*. A private sommelier wasn’t included, but if Jeff had asked, they might’ve produced one anyway.

Sherry held her cup delicately, studying the clarity of the pour. One sip confirmed what she suspected: this was real wine, not stadium juice. She caught herself smiling. Of course it was. This wasn’t just baseball. This was a transaction. This was courting. The Reds wanted the band to come back.

And if you wanted a whale to swim in your waters again, you damn well made the ocean feel like home.

---

Kathy sipped her wine with casual elegance, but her eyes never left Sherry. From across the suite, she watched like a strategist surveying terrain. She wasn’t drinking in the game, not the ballpark, not the crowd—just Sherry. Every glance, every laugh, every brush of her fingers against Jeff’s arm was logged, assessed.

This wasn’t idle jealousy. This was calculated hunger.

Kathy had known Jeff too long, too intimately, not to recognize the tone he used with this one. It wasn’t just sex. It wasn’t even just comfort. It was reverence. *Reverence.* Kathy hadn’t seen that since… well, maybe ever. And it wasn’t that she wanted Jeff back, not really. She didn’t need him. But if he could *worship* this woman, if this plainclothes, civilian-blooded accountant could awaken that kind of response, then Kathy wanted to understand it. *Possess* it.

She was already rehearsing the wedge—an angle of approach that didn’t scream aggression or insecurity. Something soft. Something that would allow her to ease her way into Sherry’s confidence. A compliment too specific to be fake. A shared joke. Maybe even just a lingering touch of the hand.

Kathy had turned straighter women. Not many, but enough to know that it was never about the gender—it was about the gravity. And Sherry? Sherry was teetering. The way her eyes drifted. The flushed surprise when Kathy walked in. The way she’d fled to the bathroom with trembling fingers.

She could feel it. She could smell it. Jeff’s toy wasn’t just vulnerable—she was *curious*.

And Kathy, with all her red wrap and slow-burning magnetism, would be the answer to that curiosity. She just had to wait for the crack. The precise moment Sherry leaned an inch too far.

That was when Kathy would slip in.

And take what she wanted.

---

Kathy swirled the last of her wine in the bottom of the glass, eyes locked on Sherry as if she were appraising a priceless painting—something rare, something maybe misframed, but undeniably *valuable*. She could feel it deep in her gut: this wasn’t just a flirtation anymore. This was a narrow window, closing fast.

If she didn’t act today—*now*, even—she’d lose the chance. Sherry still had that raw openness, that inner coil of conflict that betrayed someone not yet settled in her identity. But the clock was ticking. Kathy could *see* the way Jeff looked at her, the glances that lingered a little too long, the subtle protectiveness that clung to his movements. And Sherry, in her jeans and her wariness, wasn’t entirely sure whether to lean into it or run.

That made her *vulnerable*. That made her *reachable*.

But if Kathy waited too long—if she missed this game, this suite, this very moment—she’d be shaking hands with *Mrs. Evans* next time, and all the doors would slam shut. She’d be out of bounds. Jeff would mark his territory, and Sherry would fall in line, armored by commitment and the dull comfort of monogamy.

No. It had to be today.

She needed something subtle, something casual. Just a number. That was all. A text to follow up on some laugh they shared. A promise to send a link to that insane Tokyo sushi spot Jeff probably hadn’t shut up about. Something *harmless* on its face. But with potential. So much potential.

Because Kathy wasn’t trying to blow up their world. She just wanted a taste. A moment. A lazy afternoon, sometime this spring. Maybe a bottle of wine. Maybe less clothing. Just a little sip of the woman Jeff held in such high regard.

After all, Kathy believed in sharing the finest things in life. Especially when they didn’t even realize how rare they were.

---
